Les Miserables	﻿les misérables   by victor hugo   part premier  fantine  authorized translation by sir lascelles wraxall.
Les Miserables	_boston:_  little, brown, and company.
Les Miserables	1887    [illustration: victor hugo (1828)]     publishers' preface.
Les Miserables	the present edition of "les misérables," in five volumes, has been made with the special object of supplying the work in a proper form for library use, embodying the two great requisites, clear type and handy size.
Les Miserables	it is in the main a reprint of the english translation, in three volumes, by sir lascelles wraxall, which was made with the sanction and advice of the author.
Les Miserables	chapters and passages omitted in the english edition have been specially translated for the present issue; numerous errors of the press, etc., have been corrected; and the author's own arrangement of the work in five parts, and his subdivisions into books and chapters, have been restored.
Les Miserables	boston, _sept_.
Les Miserables	1, 1887.     preface   so long as, by the effect of laws and of customs, social degradation shall continue in the midst of civilization, making artificial hells, and subjecting to the complications of chance the divine destiny of man; so long as the three problems of the age,--the debasement of man by the proletariat, the ruin of woman by the force of hunger, the destruction of children in the darkness,--shall not be solved; so long as anywhere social syncope shall be possible: in other words, and from a still broader point of view, so long as ignorance and misery shall remain on earth, books like this cannot fail to be useful.

Les Miserables	fantine.
Les Miserables	book i.   a just man.
Les Miserables	chapter i.   m. myriel.
Les Miserables	in 1815 m. charles françois bienvenu myriel was bishop of d----.
Les Miserables	he was a man of about seventy-five years of age, and had held the see of d---- since 1806. although the following details in no way affect our narrative, it may not be useless to quote the rumors that were current about him at the moment when he came to the diocese, for what is said of men, whether it be true or false, often occupies as much space in their life, and especially in their destiny, as what they do.
Les Miserables	m. myriel was the son of a councillor of the aix parliament.
Les Miserables	it was said that his father, who intended that he should be his successor, married him at the age of eighteen or twenty, according to a not uncommon custom in parliamentary families.
Les Miserables	charles myriel, in spite of this marriage (so people said), had been the cause of much tattle.
Les Miserables	he was well built, though of short stature, elegant, graceful, and witty; and the earlier part of his life was devoted to the world and to gallantry.
Les Miserables	the revolution came, events hurried on, and the parliamentary families, decimated and hunted down, became dispersed.
Les Miserables	m. charles myriel emigrated to italy in the early part of the revolution, and his wife, who had been long suffering from a chest complaint, died there, leaving no children.
Les Miserables	what next took place in m. myriel's destiny?
Les Miserables	did the overthrow of the old french society, the fall of his own family, and the tragic spectacles of '93, more frightful perhaps to the emigrés who saw them from a distance with the magnifying power of terror, cause ideas of renunciation and solitude to germinate in him?
Les Miserables	was he, in the midst of one of the distractions and affections which occupied his life, suddenly assailed by one of those mysterious and terrible blows which often prostrate, by striking at his heart, a man whom public catastrophes could not overthrow by attacking him in his existence and his fortune?
Les Miserables	no one could have answered these questions; all that was known was that when he returned from italy he was a priest.
Les Miserables	in 1804 m. myriel was curé of b---- (brignolles).
Les Miserables	he was already aged, and lived in great retirement.
Les Miserables	towards the period of the coronation a small matter connected with his curacy, no one remembers what, took him to paris.
Les Miserables	among other powerful persons he applied to cardinal fesch on behalf of his parishioners.
Les Miserables	one day, when the emperor was paying a visit to his uncle, the worthy curé, who was waiting in the ante-room, saw his majesty pass.
Les Miserables	napoleon, noticing this old man regard him with some degree of curiosity, turned and asked sharply,--  "who is this good man who is staring at me?"
Les Miserables	"sire," m. myriel said, "you are looking at a good man and i at a great man.
Les Miserables	we may both profit by it."
Les Miserables	the emperor, on the same evening, asked the cardinal the curé's name, and some time after m. myriel, to his great surprise, learned that he was nominated bishop of d----.
Les Miserables	what truth, by the way, was there in the stories about m. myriel's early life?
Les Miserables	no one knew, for few persons had been acquainted with his family before the revolution.
Les Miserables	m. myriel was fated to undergo the lot of every new comer to a little town, where there are many mouths that speak, and but few heads that think.
Les Miserables	he was obliged to undergo it, though he was bishop, and because he was bishop.
Les Miserables	but, after all, the stories in which his name was mingled were only stories, rumors, words, remarks, less than words, mere _palabres_, to use a term borrowed from the energetic language of the south.
Les Miserables	whatever they might be, after ten years of episcopacy and residence at d----, all this gossip, which at the outset affords matter of conversation for little towns and little people, had fallen into deep oblivion.
Les Miserables	no one would have dared to speak of it, no one have dared to remember it.
Les Miserables	m. myriel had arrived at d----, accompanied by an old maid, mlle.
Les Miserables	baptistine, who was his sister, and ten years younger than himself.
Les Miserables	their only servant was a female of the same age as mademoiselle, of the name of madame magloire, who, after having been the servant of m. le curé, now assumed the double title of waiting-woman to mademoiselle, and house-keeper to monseigneur.
Les Miserables	mlle.
Les Miserables	baptistine was a tall, pale, slim, gentle person; she realized the ideal of what the word "respectable" expresses, for it seems necessary for a woman to be a mother in order to be venerable.
Les Miserables	she had never been pretty, but her whole life, which had been but a succession of pious works, had eventually cast over her a species of whiteness and brightness, and in growing older she had acquired what may be called the beauty of goodness.
Les Miserables	what had been thinness in her youth had become in her maturity transparency, and through this transparency the angel could be seen.
Les Miserables	she seemed to be a shadow, there was hardly enough body for a sex to exist; she was a little quantity of matter containing a light--an excuse for a soul to remain upon the earth.
Les Miserables	madame magloire was a fair, plump, busy little body, always short of breath,--in the first place, through her activity, and, secondly, in consequence of an asthma.
Les Miserables	on his arrival m. myriel was installed in his episcopal palace with all the honors allotted by the imperial decrees which classify the bishop immediately after a major-general.
Les Miserables	the mayor and the president paid him the first visit, and he on his side paid the first visit to the general and the prefect.
Les Miserables	when the installation was ended the town waited to see its bishop at work.
Les Miserables	chapter ii.
Les Miserables	m. myriel becomes monseigneur welcome.
Les Miserables	the episcopal palace of d---- adjoined the hospital.
Les Miserables	it was a spacious, handsome mansion, built at the beginning of the last century by monseigneur henri puget, doctor in theology of the faculty of paris, and abbé of simore, who was bishop of d---- in 1712. this palace was a true seigneurial residence: everything had a noble air in it,--the episcopal apartments, the reception rooms, the bed-rooms, the court of honor, which was very wide, with arcades after the old florentine fashion, and the gardens planted with magnificent trees.
Les Miserables	in the dining-room, a long and superb gallery on the ground floor, monseigneur henri puget had given a state dinner on july 29, 1714, to messeigneurs charles brûlart de genlis, archbishop, prince of embrun; antoine de mesgrigny, capuchin and bishop of grasse; philip de vendôme, grand prior of france and abbé of st. honoré de lérins; françois de berton de grillon, baron and bishop of vence; cæsar de sabran de forcalquier, bishop and lord of glandève, and jean soanen, priest of the oratory, preacher in ordinary to the king, and bishop and lord of senez.
Les Miserables	the portraits of these seven reverend personages decorated the dining-room, and the memorable date, july 29, 1714, was engraved in golden letters on a white marble tablet.
Les Miserables	the hospital was a small, single-storeyed house with a little garden.
Les Miserables	three days after his arrival the bishop visited it, and when his visit was over asked the director to be kind enough to come to his house.
Les Miserables	"how many patients have you at this moment?"
Les Miserables	he asked.
Les Miserables	"twenty-six, monseigneur."
Les Miserables	"the number i counted," said the bishop.
Les Miserables	"the beds are very close together," the director continued.
Les Miserables	"i noticed it."
Les Miserables	"the wards are only bed-rooms, and difficult to ventilate."
Les Miserables	"i thought so."
Les Miserables	"and then, when the sun shines, the garden is very small for the convalescents."
Les Miserables	"i said so to myself."
Les Miserables	"during epidemics, and we have had the typhus this year, and had miliary fever two years ago, we have as many as one hundred patients, and do not know what to do with them."
Les Miserables	"that thought occurred to me."
Les Miserables	"what would you have, monseigneur!"
Les Miserables	the director said, "we must put up with it."
Les Miserables	this conversation had taken place in the dining-hall on the ground floor.
Les Miserables	the bishop was silent for a moment, and then turned smartly to the director.
Les Miserables	"how many beds," he asked him, "do you think that this room alone would hold?"
Les Miserables	"monseigneur's dining-room?"
Les Miserables	the stupefied director asked.
Les Miserables	the bishop looked round the room, and seemed to be estimating its capacity.
Les Miserables	"it would hold twenty beds," he said, as if speaking to himself, and then, raising his voice, he added,--  "come, director, i will tell you what it is.
Les Miserables	there is evidently a mistake.
Les Miserables	you have twenty-six persons in five or six small rooms.
Les Miserables	there are only three of us, and we have room for fifty.
Les Miserables	there is a mistake, i repeat; you have my house and i have yours.
Les Miserables	restore me mine; this is yours."
Les Miserables	the next day the twenty-six poor patients were installed in the bishop's palace, and the bishop was in the hospital.
Les Miserables	m. myriel had no property, as his family had been ruined by the revolution.
Les Miserables	his sister had an annuity of 500 francs, which had sufficed at the curacy for personal expenses.
Les Miserables	m. myriel, as bishop, received from the state 15,000 francs a year.
Les Miserables	on the same day that he removed to the hospital, m. myriel settled the employment of that sum once for all in the following way.
Les Miserables	we copy here a note in his own handwriting.
Les Miserables	note for regulating my household expenses.
Les Miserables	for the little seminary                                 1500 francs.
Les Miserables	congregation of the mission                              100   -- for the lazarists of montdidier                          100   -- seminary of foreign missions at paris                    200   -- congregation of saint esprit                             150   -- religious establishments in the holy land                100   -- societies of maternal charity                            300   -- additional for the one at aries                           50 francs works for improvement of prisons                         400   -- relief and deliverance of prisoners                      500   -- for liberation of fathers of family imprisoned for debt 1000   -- addition to the salary of poor schoolmasters in the diocese                                             2000   -- distribution of grain in the upper alps                  100   -- ladies' society for gratuitous instruction of poor girls at d----, manosque, and sisteron                  1500   -- for the poor                                            6000   -- personal expenses                                       1000   --  total                                                 15,000   --  during the whole time he held the see of d----, m. myriel made no change in this arrangement.
Les Miserables	he called this, as we see, regulating his household expenses.
Les Miserables	the arrangement was accepted with a smile by mlle.
Les Miserables	baptistine, for that sainted woman regarded m. myriel at once as her brother and her bishop; her friend according to nature, her superior according to the church.
Les Miserables	she loved and venerated him in the simplest way.
Les Miserables	when he spoke she bowed, when he acted she assented.
Les Miserables	the servant alone, madame magloire, murmured a little.
Les Miserables	the bishop, it will have been noticed, only reserved 1000 francs, and on this sum, with mlle.
Les Miserables	baptistine's pension, these two old women and old man lived.
Les Miserables	and when a village curé came to d-, the bishop managed to regale him, thanks to the strict economy of madame magloire and the sensible management of mlle.
Les Miserables	baptistine.
Les Miserables	one day, when he had been at d---- about three months, the bishop said,--  "for all that, i am dreadfully pressed."
Les Miserables	"i should think so," exclaimed madame magloire.
Les Miserables	"monseigneur has not even claimed the allowance which the department is bound to pay for keeping up his carriage in town, and for his visitations.
Les Miserables	that was the custom with bishops in other times."
Les Miserables	"true," said the bishop, "you are right, madame magloire."
Les Miserables	he made his claim, and shortly after the council-general, taking the demand into consideration, voted him the annual sum of 3000 francs, under the heading, "allowance to the bishop for maintenance of carriage, posting charges, and outlay in visitations."
Les Miserables	this caused an uproar among the cits of the town, and on this occasion a senator of the empire, ex-member of the council of the five hundred, favourable to the 18th brumaire, and holding a magnificent appointment near d----, wrote to the minister of worship, m. bigot de préameneu, a short, angry, and confidential letter, from which we extract these authentic lines:  "----maintenance of carriage!
Les Miserables	what can he want one for in a town of less than 4000 inhabitants?
Les Miserables	visitation charges!
Les Miserables	in the first place, what is the good of visitations at all?
Les Miserables	and, secondly, how can he travel post in this mountainous country, where there are no roads, and people must travel on horseback?
Les Miserables	the very bridge over the durance at château arnoux can hardly bear the weight of a cart drawn by oxen.
Les Miserables	these priests are all the same, greedy and avaricious!
Les Miserables	this one played the good apostle when he arrived, but now he is like the rest, and must have his carriage and post-chaise.
Les Miserables	he wishes to be as luxurious as the old bishops.
Les Miserables	oh this priesthood!
Les Miserables	my lord, matters will never go on well till the emperor has delivered us from the skullcaps.
Les Miserables	down with the pope!
Les Miserables	(there was a quarrel at the time with rome).
Les Miserables	as for me, i am for cæsar and cæsar alone, etc., etc., etc."
Les Miserables	the affair, on the other hand, greatly gladdened madame magloire.
Les Miserables	"come," she said to mlle.
Les Miserables	baptistine, "monseigneur began with others, but he was obliged to finish with himself.
Les Miserables	he has regulated all his charities, and here are 3000 francs for us at last!"
Les Miserables	the same evening the bishop wrote, and gave his sister, a note conceived thus:--  carriage and travelling expenses.
Les Miserables	to provide the hospital patients with broth     1500 francs.
Les Miserables	the society of maternal charity at aix           250   -- the society of maternal charity at draguignan    250   -- for foundlings                                   500   -- for orphans                                      500   -- total                                           3000   --  such was m. myriel's budget.
Les Miserables	as for the accidental receipts, such as fees for bans, christenings, consecrating churches or chapels, marriages, &c., the bishop collected them from the rich with so much the more eagerness because he distributed them to the poor.
Les Miserables	in a short time the monetary offerings became augmented.
Les Miserables	those who have and those who want tapped at m. myriel's door, the last coming to seek the alms which the former had just deposited.
Les Miserables	the bishop in less than a year became the treasurer of all charity and the cashier of all distress.
Les Miserables	considerable sums passed through his hands, but nothing could induce him to make any change in his mode of life, or add the slightest superfluity to his expenditure.
Les Miserables	far from it, as there is always more wretchedness at the bottom than paternity above, all was given, so to speak, before being received; it was like water on dry ground: however much he might receive he had never a farthing.
Les Miserables	at such times he stripped himself.
Les Miserables	it being the custom for the bishops to place their christian names at the head of their mandates and pastoral letters, the poor people of the country had selected the one among them which conveyed a meaning, and called him monseigneur welcome (bienvenu).
Les Miserables	we will do like them, and call him so when occasion serves.
Les Miserables	moreover, the name pleased him.
Les Miserables	"i like that name," he would say.
Les Miserables	"the welcome corrects the monseigneur."
Les Miserables	we do not assert that the portrait we are here drawing is probably as far as fiction goes: we confine ourselves to saying that it bears a likeness to the reality.
Les Miserables	chapter iii.
Les Miserables	a good bishop and a hard bishopric.
Les Miserables	the bishop, though he had converted his coach into alms, did not the less make his visitations.
Les Miserables	the diocese of d---- is fatiguing; there are few plains and many mountains, and hardly any roads, as we saw just now: twenty-two curacies, forty-one vicarages, and two hundred and eighty-five chapels of ease.
Les Miserables	it was a task to visit all these, but the bishop managed it.
Les Miserables	he went on foot when the place was near, in a carriage when it was in the plain, and on a mule when it was in the mountains.
Les Miserables	the two old females generally accompanied him, but when the journey was too wearying for them he went alone.
Les Miserables	one day he arrived at senez, which is an old episcopal town, mounted on a donkey; his purse, which was very light at the time, had not allowed him any other equipage.
Les Miserables	the mayor of the city came to receive him at the door of the bishop's palace, and saw him dismount with scandalized eyes.
Les Miserables	a few cits were laughing round him.
Les Miserables	"m. mayor and gentlemen," the bishop said, "i see what it is that scandalizes you.
Les Miserables	you consider it great pride for a poor priest to ride an animal which our saviour once upon a time bestrode.
Les Miserables	i did so through necessity, i assure you, and not through vanity."
Les Miserables	on his tours the bishop was indulgent and gentle, and preached less than he conversed.
Les Miserables	his reasonings and models were never far-fetched, and to the inhabitants of one country he quoted the example of an adjacent country.
Les Miserables	in those cantons where people were harsh to the needy he would say, "look at the people of briançon.
Les Miserables	they have given the indigent, the widows, and the orphans, the right of mowing their fields three days before all the rest.
Les Miserables	they rebuild their houses gratuitously when they are in ruins.
Les Miserables	hence it is a country blessed of god.
Les Miserables	for one hundred years not a single murder has been committed there."
Les Miserables	to those eager for grain and good crops, he said, "look at the people of embrun.
Les Miserables	if a father of a family at harvest-time has his sons in the army, his daughters serving in the town, or if he be ill or prevented from toil, the curé recommends him in his sermon; and on sunday after mass all the villagers, men, women, and children, go into his field, and cut and carry home his crop."
Les Miserables	to families divided by questions of money or inheritance he said, "look at the highlanders of devolny, a country so wild that the nightingale is not heard once in fifty years.
Les Miserables	well, when the father of a family dies there the boys go off to seek their fortune, and leave the property to the girls, so that they may obtain husbands."
Les Miserables	in those parts where the farmers are fond of lawsuits, and ruin themselves in writs, he would say, "look at those good peasants of the valley of queyras.
Les Miserables	there are three thousand souls there.
Les Miserables	why, it is like a little republic.
Les Miserables	neither judge nor bailiff is known there, and the mayor does everything.
Les Miserables	he divides the imposts, taxes everybody conscientiously, settles quarrels gratis, allots patrimonies without fees, gives sentences without costs, and is obeyed because he is a just man among simple men."
Les Miserables	in villages where there was no schoolmaster he again quoted the people of queyras.
Les Miserables	"do you know what they do?
Les Miserables	as a small place, containing only twelve or fifteen hearths, cannot always support a master, they have schoolmasters paid by the whole valley, who go from village to village, spending a week in one, ten days in another, and teaching.
Les Miserables	these masters go the fairs, where i have seen them.
Les Miserables	they can be recognized by the pens they carry in their hat-band.
Les Miserables	those who only teach reading have but one pen: those who teach reading and arithmetic have two: those who teach reading, arithmetic, and latin, have three.
Les Miserables	but what a disgrace it is to be ignorant!
Les Miserables	do like the people of queyras."
Les Miserables	he spoke thus, gravely and paternally.
Les Miserables	when examples failed him he invented parables, going straight to the point, with few phrases and a good deal of imagery.
Les Miserables	his was the eloquence of the apostles, convincing and persuading.
Les Miserables	chapter iv.
Les Miserables	works resembling words.
Les Miserables	the bishop's conversation was affable and lively.
Les Miserables	he condescended to the level of the two old females who spent their life near him, and when he laughed it was a schoolboy's laugh.
Les Miserables	madame magloire was fond of calling him "your grandeur."
Les Miserables	one day he rose from his easy chair and went to fetch a book from his library: as it was on one of the top shelves, and as the bishop was short, he could not reach it "madame magloire," he said, "bring me a chair, for my grandeur does not rise to that shelf."
Les Miserables	one of his distant relatives, the countess de lô, rarely let an opportunity slip to enumerate in his presence what she called the "hopes" of her three sons.
Les Miserables	she had several very old relatives close to death's door, of whom her sons were the natural heirs.
Les Miserables	the youngest of the three would inherit from a great-aunt 100,000 francs a year; the second would succeed to his uncle's dukedom, the third to his grandfather's peerage.
Les Miserables	the bishop generally listened in silence to this innocent and pardonable maternal display.
Les Miserables	once, however, he seemed more dreamy than usual, while madame de lô was repeating all the details of their successions and "hopes."
Les Miserables	she broke off somewhat impatiently.
Les Miserables	"good gracious, cousin," she said, "what are you thinking, about?"
Les Miserables	"i am thinking," said the bishop, "of something singular, which, if my memory is right, is in st. augustine.
Les Miserables	place your hopes in the man to whom it is impossible to succeed."
Les Miserables	on another occasion, receiving a letter announcing the death of a country gentleman, in which, in addition to the dignities of the defunct, all the feudal and noble titles of all his relatives were recorded,--"what a back death has!
Les Miserables	what an admirable burthen of titles he is made lightly to bear," he exclaimed, "and what sense men must possess thus to employ the tomb in satisfying their vanity."
Les Miserables	he displayed at times a gentle raillery, which nearly always contained a serious meaning.
Les Miserables	during one lent a young vicar came to d---- and preached at the cathedral.
Les Miserables	he was rather eloquent, and the subject of his sermon was charity.
Les Miserables	he invited the rich to give to the needy in order to escape hell, which he painted in the most frightful way he could, and reach paradise, which he made desirable and charming.
Les Miserables	there was among the congregation a rich, retired merchant, somewhat of a usurer, who had acquired two million francs by manufacturing coarse cloths, serges, and caddis.
Les Miserables	in his whole life-time m. géborand had never given alms to a beggar, but after this sermon it was remarked that he gave every sunday a sou to the old women begging at the cathedral gate.
Les Miserables	there were six of them to share it.
Les Miserables	one day the bishop saw him bestowing his charity, and said to his sister, with a smile, "look at m. géborand buying heaven for a sou."
Les Miserables	when it was a question of charity he would not let himself be rebuffed even by a refusal, and at such times made remarks which caused people to reflect.
Les Miserables	once he was collecting for the poor in a drawing-room of the town.
Les Miserables	the marquis de champtercier was present, a rich old avaricious man, who contrived to be at once ultra-royalist and ultra-voltairian.
Les Miserables	this variety has existed.
Les Miserables	the bishop on reaching him touched his arm, "monsieur le marquis, you must give me something."
Les Miserables	the marquis turned and answered dryly: "i have my own poor, monseigneur."
Les Miserables	"give them to me," said the bishop.
Les Miserables	one day he delivered the following sermon at the cathedral:--  "my very dear brethren, my good friends, there are in france thirteen hundred and twenty thousand peasants' houses which have only three openings; eighteen hundred and seventeen thousand which have only two openings, the door and the window; and, lastly, three hundred and forty-six thousand cabins which have only one opening, the door, and this is because of a thing called the door and window tax.
Les Miserables	just place poor families, aged women and little children, in these houses, and then see the fevers and maladies!
Les Miserables	alas!
Les Miserables	god gives men fresh air, and the law sells it to them.
Les Miserables	i do not accuse the law, but i bless god.
Les Miserables	in the isère, in the var, in the two alps, upper and lower, the peasants have not even trucks, but carry manure on their backs: they have no candles, and burn resinous logs and pieces of rope steeped in pitch.
Les Miserables	it is the same through all the high parts of dauphiné.
Les Miserables	they make bread for six months, and bake it with dried cow-dung.
Les Miserables	in winter they break this bread with axes and steep it in water for four-and-twenty hours before they can eat it.
Les Miserables	brethren, have pity, see how people suffer around you!"
Les Miserables	a provençal by birth, he easily accustomed himself to all the dialects of the south: this greatly pleased the people, and had done no little in securing him admission to all minds.
Les Miserables	he was, as it were, at home in the hut and on the mountain.
Les Miserables	he could say the grandest things in the most vulgar idioms, and as he spoke all languages he entered all hearts.
Les Miserables	however, he was the same to people of fashion as to the lower classes.
Les Miserables	he never condemned anything hastily or without taking the circumstances into calculation.
Les Miserables	he would say, let us look at the road by which the fault has come.
Les Miserables	being, as he called himself with a smile, an ex-sinner, he had none of the intrenchments of rigorism, and, careless of the frowns of the unco' good, professed loudly a doctrine which might be summed up nearly as follows,--  "man has upon him the flesh which is at once his burden and his temptation.
Les Miserables	he carries it with him and yields to it.
Les Miserables	he must watch, restrain, and repress it, and only obey it in the last extremity.
Les Miserables	in this obedience there may still be a fault: but the fault thus committed is venial.
Les Miserables	it is a fall, but a fall on the knees, which may end in prayer.
Les Miserables	to be a saint is the exception, to be a just man is the rule.
Les Miserables	err, fail, sin, but be just.
Les Miserables	the least possible amount of sin is the law of man: no sin at all is the dream of angels.
Les Miserables	all that is earthly is subjected to sin, for sin is a gravitation."
Les Miserables	when he saw everybody cry out and grow indignant, all of a sudden, he would say with a smile, "oh!
Les Miserables	oh, it seems as if this is a great crime which all the world is committing.
Les Miserables	look at the startled hypocrites, hastening to protest and place themselves under cover."
Les Miserables	he was indulgent to the women and the poor on whom the weight of human society presses.
Les Miserables	he would say, "the faults of women, children, servants, the weak, the indigent, and the ignorant are the fault of husbands, fathers, masters, the strong, the rich, and the learned."
Les Miserables	he also said, "teach the ignorant as much as you possibly can: society is culpable for not giving instruction gratis, and is responsible for the night it produces.
Les Miserables	this soul is full of darkness, and sin is committed, but the guilty person is not the man who commits the sin, but he who produces the darkness."
Les Miserables	as we see, he had a strange manner, peculiarly his own, of judging things.
Les Miserables	i suspect that he obtained it from the gospels.
Les Miserables	he one day heard in a drawing-room the story of a trial which was shortly to take place.
Les Miserables	a wretched man, through love of a woman and a child he had by her, having exhausted his resources, coined false money, which at that period was an offence punished by death.
Les Miserables	the woman was arrested while issuing the first false piece manufactured by the man.
Les Miserables	she was detained, but there was no proof against her.
Les Miserables	she alone could accuse her lover and ruin him by confessing.
Les Miserables	she denied.
Les Miserables	they pressed her, but she adhered to her denial.
Les Miserables	upon this, the attorney for the crown had an idea: he feigned infidelity on the lover's part, and contrived, by cleverly presenting the woman with fragments of letters, to persuade her that she had a rival, and that the man was deceiving her.
Les Miserables	then, exasperated by jealousy, she denounced her lover, confessed everything, proved everything.
Les Miserables	the man was ruined, and would shortly be tried with his accomplice at aix.
Les Miserables	the story was told, and everybody was delighted at the magistrate's cleverness.
Les Miserables	by bringing jealousy into play he brought out the truth through passion, and obtained justice through revenge.
Les Miserables	the bishop listened to all this in silence, and when it was ended he asked: "where will this man and woman be tried?"
Les Miserables	"at the assizes."
Les Miserables	then he continued, "and where will the attorney for the crown be tried?"
Les Miserables	a tragical event occurred at d----.
Les Miserables	a man was condemned to death for murder.
Les Miserables	he was a wretched fellow, not exactly educated, not exactly ignorant, who had been a mountebank at fairs and a public writer.
Les Miserables	the trial attracted the attention of the towns-people.
Les Miserables	on the eve of the day fixed for the execution the prison chaplain was taken ill, and a priest was wanted to assist the sufferer in his last moments.
Les Miserables	the curé was sent for, and it seems that he refused, saying, "it is no business of mine, i have nothing to do with the mountebank, i am ill too, and besides, that is not my place."
Les Miserables	this answer was carried to the bishop, who said, "the curé is right, it is not his place, it is mine."
Les Miserables	he went straight to the prison, entered the mountebank's cell, called him by name, took his hand, and spoke to him.
Les Miserables	he spent the whole day with him, forgetting sleep and food while praying to god for the soul of the condemned man.
Les Miserables	he told him the best truths, which are the most simple.
Les Miserables	he was father, brother, friend--bishop only to bless.
Les Miserables	he taught him everything, while reassuring and consoling him.
Les Miserables	this man was about to die in desperation: death was to him like an abyss, and he shuddered as he stood on its gloomy brink.
Les Miserables	he was not ignorant enough to be completely indifferent, and his condemnation, which was a profound shock, had here and there broken through that partition which separates us from the mystery of things, and which we call life.
Les Miserables	he peered incessantly out of this world through these crevices, and only saw darkness; but the bishop showed him a light.
Les Miserables	on the morrow, when they came to fetch the condemned man, the bishop was with him.
Les Miserables	he followed him, and showed himself to the mob in his purple cassock, and with the episcopal cross round his neck, side by side with this rope-bound wretch.
Les Miserables	he entered the cart with him, he mounted the scaffold with him.
Les Miserables	the sufferer, so gloomy and crushed on the previous day, was radiant; he felt that his soul was reconciled, and he hoped for heaven.
Les Miserables	the bishop embraced him, and at the moment when the knife was about to fall, said: "the man whom his fellow-men kill, god resuscitates.
Les Miserables	he whom his brothers expel finds the father again.
Les Miserables	pray, believe, enter into life!
Les Miserables	the father is there!"
Les Miserables	when he descended from the scaffold there was something in his glance which made the people open a path for him; it was impossible to say whether his pallor or his serenity were the more admirable.
Les Miserables	on returning to the humble abode, which he called smilingly his palace, he said to his sister: "i have just been officiating pontifically."
Les Miserables	as the most sublime things are often those least understood, there were persons in the town who said, in commenting on the bishop's conduct, "it is affectation."
Les Miserables	this, however, was only the talk of drawing-rooms; the people who do not regard holy actions with suspicion were affected, and admired.
Les Miserables	as for the bishop, the sight of the guillotine was a shock to him, and it was long ere he recovered from it.
Les Miserables	the scaffold, in fact, when it stands erect before you, has something about it that hallucinates.
Les Miserables	we may feel a certain amount of indifference about the punishment of death, not express an opinion, and say yes or no, so long as we have never seen a guillotine; but when we have come across one the shock is violent, and we must decide either for or against.
Les Miserables	some admire it, like de maistre, others execrate it, like beccaria.
Les Miserables	the guillotine is the concretion of the law, it calls itself _vindicta_; it is not neutral, and does not allow you to remain neutral.
Les Miserables	the person who perceives it shudders with the most mysterious of shudders.
Les Miserables	all the social questions raise their notes of interrogation round this cutter.
Les Miserables	the scaffold is a vision, it is not carpenter's work, it is not a machine, it is not a lifeless mechanism made of wood, steel, and ropes.
Les Miserables	it seems to be a species of being possessing a gloomy intuition; you might say that the wood-work lives, that the machine hears, that the mechanism understands, that the wood, the steel, and the ropes, have a volition.
Les Miserables	in the frightful reverie into which its presence casts the mind the scaffold appears terrible, and mixed up with what it does.
Les Miserables	the scaffold is the accomplice of the executioner; it devours, it eats flesh and drinks blood.
Les Miserables	the scaffold is a species of monster, manufactured by the judge and the carpenter, a spectre that seems to live a sort of horrible life made up of all the death it has produced.
Les Miserables	hence the impression was terrible and deep; on the day after the execution, and for many days beyond, the bishop appeared crushed.
Les Miserables	the almost violent serenity of the mournful moment had departed; the phantom of social justice haunted him.
Les Miserables	he who usually returned from all his duties with such radiant satisfaction seemed to be reproaching himself.
Les Miserables	at times he soliloquized, and stammered unconnected sentences in a low voice.
Les Miserables	here is one which his sister overheard and treasured up: "i did not believe that it was so monstrous.
Les Miserables	it is wrong to absorb oneself in the divine law so greatly as no longer to perceive the human law.
Les Miserables	death belongs to god alone.
Les Miserables	by what right do men touch that unknown thing?"
Les Miserables	with time these impressions were attenuated, and perhaps effaced.
Les Miserables	still it was noticed that from this period the bishop avoided crossing the execution square.
Les Miserables	m. myriel might be called at any hour to the bedside of the sick and the dying.
Les Miserables	he was not ignorant that his greatest duty and greatest labor lay there.
Les Miserables	widowed or orphaned families had no occasion to send for him, for he came of himself.
Les Miserables	he had the art of sitting down and holding his tongue for hours by the side of a man who had lost the wife he loved, or of a mother bereaved of her child.
Les Miserables	as he knew the time to be silent, he also knew the time to speak.
Les Miserables	what an admirable consoler he was!
Les Miserables	he did not try to efface grief by oblivion, but to aggrandize and dignify it by hope.
Les Miserables	he would say: "take care of the way in which you turn to the dead.
Les Miserables	do not think of that which perishes.
Les Miserables	look fixedly, and you will perceive the living light of your beloved dead in heaven."
Les Miserables	he knew that belief is healthy, and he sought to counsel and calm the desperate man by pointing out to him the resigned man, and to transform the grief that gazes at a grave by showing it the grief that looks at a star.
Les Miserables	chapter v.   monseigneur's cassocks last too long.
Les Miserables	m. myriel's domestic life was full of the same thoughts as his public life.
Les Miserables	to any one who could inspect it closely, the voluntary poverty in which the bishop lived would have been a solemn and charming spectacle.
Les Miserables	like all old men, and like most thinkers, he slept little, but that short sleep was deep.
Les Miserables	in the morning he remained in contemplation for an hour, and then read mass either at the cathedral or in his house.
Les Miserables	mass over, he breakfasted on rye bread dipped in the milk of his own cows.
Les Miserables	then he set to work.
Les Miserables	a bishop is a very busy man.
Les Miserables	he must daily receive the secretary to the bishopric, who is generally a canon, and almost every day his grand vicars.
Les Miserables	he has congregations to control, permissions to grant, a whole ecclesiastical library to examine, in the shape of diocesan catechisms, books of hours, etc.
Les Miserables	; mandates to write, sermons to authorize, curés and mayors to reconcile, a clerical correspondence, an administrative correspondence, on one side the state, on the other the holy see; in a word, a thousand tasks.
Les Miserables	the time which these thousand tasks, his offices, and his breviary left him, he gave first to the needy, the sick, and the afflicted; the time which the afflicted, the sick, and the needy left him he gave to work.
Les Miserables	sometimes he hoed in his garden, at others he read and wrote.
Les Miserables	he had only one name for both sorts of labor, he called them gardening.
Les Miserables	"the mind is a garden," he would say.
Les Miserables	toward mid-day, when the weather was fine, he went out and walked in the country or the town, frequently entering the cottages.
Les Miserables	he could be seen walking alone in deep thought, looking down, leaning on his long cane, dressed in his violet wadded and warm great coat, with his violet stockings thrust into clumsy shoes, and wearing his flat hat, through each corner of which were passed three golden acorns as tassels.
Les Miserables	it was a festival wherever he appeared, it seemed as if his passing had something warming and luminous about it; old men and children came to the door to greet the bishop as they did the sun.
Les Miserables	he blessed them and they blessed him, and his house was pointed out to anybody who was in want of anything.
Les Miserables	now and then he stopped, spoke to the little boys and girls, and smiled on their mothers.
Les Miserables	he visited the poor so long as he had any money; when he had none he visited the rich.
Les Miserables	as he made his cassocks last a long time, and he did not wish the fact to be noticed, he never went into town save in his wadded violet coat.
Les Miserables	this was rather tiresome in summer.
Les Miserables	on returning home he dined.
Les Miserables	the dinner resembled the breakfast.
Les Miserables	at half-past eight in the evening he supped with his sister, madame magloire standing behind them and waiting on them.
Les Miserables	nothing could be more frugal than this meal; but if the bishop had a curé to supper, madame magloire would take advantage of it to serve monseigneur with some excellent fish from the lake, or famous game from the mountain.
Les Miserables	every curé was the excuse for a good meal, and the bishop held his tongue.
Les Miserables	on other occasions his repast only consisted of vegetables boiled in water and soup made with oil.
Les Miserables	hence it was said in the town: "when the bishop does not fare like a curé he fares like a trappist."
Les Miserables	after supper he conversed for half an hour with mlle.
Les Miserables	baptistine and madame magloire; then he returned to his room and began writing again, either on loose leaves or on the margin of some folio.
Les Miserables	he was well read, and a bit of a _savant_, and has left five or six curious mss.
Les Miserables	on theological subjects, among others a dissertation on the verse from genesis, "in the beginning the spirit of god moved upon the face of the waters."
Les Miserables	he compared this verse with three texts,--the arabic, which says, "the winds of god breathed;" flavius josephus, who said, "a wind from on high fell upon the earth;" and lastly the chaldaic of onkelos, "a wind coming from god breathed on the face of the waters."
Les Miserables	in another dissertation he examines the works of hugo, bishop of ptolemaïs, great-grand-uncle of him who writes this book, and he proves that to this bishop must be attributed the various opuscules published in the last century under the pseudonym of barleycourt.
Les Miserables	at times, in the midst of his reading, no matter what book he held in his hands, he would suddenly fall into a deep meditation, from which he only emerged to write a few lines on the pages of the book.
Les Miserables	these lines have frequently no connection with the book that contains them.
Les Miserables	we have before us a note written by him on the margin of a quarto entitled, "correspondence of lord germain with generals clinton and cornwallis, and the admirals of the american station.
Les Miserables	versailles, prinçot; and paris, pissot, quai des augustins."
Les Miserables	here is the note.
Les Miserables	"o thou who art!
Les Miserables	ecclesiastes calls you omnipotence; the maccabees call you creator; the epistle to the ephesians calls you liberty; baruch calls you immensity; the psalms call you wisdom and truth; st. john calls you light; the book of kings calls you lord; exodus calls you providence; leviticus, holiness; esdras, justice; creation calls you god; man calls you the father; but solomon calls you mercy, and that is the fairest of all your names."
Les Miserables	about nine o'clock the two females withdrew and went up to their bed-rooms on the first floor, leaving him alone till morning on the ground floor.
Les Miserables	here it is necessary that we should give an exact idea of the bishop's residence.
Les Miserables	chapter vi.
Les Miserables	by whom the house was guarded.
Les Miserables	the house the bishop resided in consisted, as we have said, of a ground floor and one above it, three rooms on the ground, three bed-rooms on the first floor, and above them a store-room.
Les Miserables	behind the house was a quarter of an acre of garden.
Les Miserables	the two females occupied the first floor, and the bishop lodged below.
Les Miserables	the first room, which opened on the street, served him as dining-room, the second as bed-room, the third as oratory.
Les Miserables	you could not get out of the oratory without passing through the bed-room, or out of the bed-room without passing through the sitting-room.
Les Miserables	at the end of the oratory was a closed alcove with a bed, for any one who stayed the night, and the bishop offered this bed to country curés whom business or the calls of their parish brought to d----.
Les Miserables	the hospital surgery, a small building added to the house and built on a part of the garden, had been transformed into kitchen and cellar.
Les Miserables	there was also in the garden a stable, which had been the old hospital kitchen, and in which the bishop kept two cows.
Les Miserables	whatever the quantity of milk they yielded, he invariably sent one half every morning to the hospital patients.
Les Miserables	"i am paying my tithes," he was wont to say.
Les Miserables	his room was rather spacious, and very difficult to heat in the cold weather.
Les Miserables	as wood is excessively dear at d----, he hit on the idea of partitioning off with planks a portion of the cow-house.
Les Miserables	here he spent his evenings during the great frosts, and called it his "winter drawing-room."
Les Miserables	in this room, as in the dining-room, there was no other furniture but a square deal table and four straw chairs.
Les Miserables	the dining-room was also adorned with an old buffet stained to imitate rosewood.
Les Miserables	the bishop had made the altar which decorated his oratory out of a similar buffet, suitably covered with white cloths and imitation lace.
Les Miserables	his rich penitents and the religious ladies of d---- had often subscribed to pay for a handsome new altar for monseigneur's oratory; each time he took the money and gave it to the poor.
Les Miserables	"the finest of all altars," he would say, "is the soul of an unhappy man who is consoled and thanks god."
Les Miserables	there were in his oratory two straw priedieus, and an arm-chair, also of straw, in his bed-room.
Les Miserables	when he by chance received seven or eight persons at the same time, the prefect, the general, the staff of the regiment quartered in the town, or some pupils of the lower seminary, it was necessary to fetch the chairs from the winter drawing-room, the priedieus from the oratory, and the easy chair from the bed-room: in this way as many as eleven seats could be collected for the visitors.
Les Miserables	at each new visit a room was unfurnished.
Les Miserables	it happened at times that there would be twelve; in such a case the bishop concealed the embarrassing nature of the situation by standing before the chimney if it were winter, or walking up and down the room were it summer.
Les Miserables	there was also another chair in the alcove, but it was half robbed of the straw, and had only three legs to stand on, so that it could only be used when resting against a wall.
Les Miserables	mlle.
Les Miserables	baptistine also had in her bed-room a very large settee of wood, which had once been gilt and covered with flowered chintz, but it had been necessary to raise this settee to the first floor through the window, owing to the narrowness of the stairs: and hence it could not be reckoned on in any emergency.
Les Miserables	it had been mlle.
Les Miserables	baptistine's ambition to buy drawing-room furniture of mahogany and covered with yellow utrecht velvet, but this would have cost at least 500 francs, and seeing that she had only succeeded in saving for this object 42 francs 5 sous in five years, she gave up the idea.
Les Miserables	besides, who is there that ever attains his ideal?
Les Miserables	nothing more simple can be imagined than the bishop's bed-room.
Les Miserables	a long window opening on the garden; opposite the bed, an iron hospital bed with a canopy of green serge; in the shadow of the bed, behind a curtain, toilet articles, still revealing the old elegant habits of the man of fashion; two doors, one near the chimney leading to the oratory, the other near the library leading to the dining-room.
Les Miserables	the library was a large glass case full of books; the chimney of wood, painted to imitate marble, was habitually fireless; in the chimney were a pair of iron andirons ornamented with two vases, displaying garlands and grooves which had once been silvered, which was a species of episcopal luxury; over the chimney a crucifix of unsilvered copper fastened to threadbare black velvet, in a frame which had lost its gilding; near the window was a large table with an inkstand, loaded with irregularly arranged papers and heavy tomes; before the table the straw arm-chair; in front of the bed a priedieu borrowed from the oratory.
Les Miserables	two portraits, in oval frames, hung on the wall on either side of the bed.
Les Miserables	small gilded inscriptions on the neutral tinted ground of the canvas by the side of the figures indicated that the portraits represented, one the abbé de chaliot, bishop of st. claude; the other the abbé tourteau, vicar-general of agde, and abbé of grand champs, belonging to the cistertian order in the diocese of chartres.
Les Miserables	the bishop, on succeeding to the hospital infirmary, found the pictures there and left them.
Les Miserables	they were priests, probably donors,--two motives for him to respect them.
Les Miserables	all he knew of the two personages was that they had been nominated by the king, the one to his bishopric, the other to his benefice, on the same day, april 27, 1785. madame magloire having unhooked the portraits to remove the dust, the bishop found this circumstance recorded in faded ink on a small square of paper which time had turned yellow, and fastened by four wafers behind the portrait of the abbé of grand champs.
Les Miserables	he had at his window an antique curtain of heavy woollen stuff, which had grown so old that madame magloire, in order to avoid the expense of a new one, was obliged to make a large seam in the very middle of it.
Les Miserables	the seam formed a cross, and the bishop often drew attention to it.
Les Miserables	"how pleasant that is," he would say.
Les Miserables	all the rooms in the house, ground floor and first floor, were white-washed, which is a barrack and hospital fashion.
Les Miserables	still, some years later, madame magloire discovered, as we shall see further on, paintings under the white-washed paper, in mlle.
Les Miserables	baptistine's bed-room.
Les Miserables	the rooms were paved with red bricks which were washed every week, and there were straw mats in front of all the beds.
Les Miserables	this house, moreover, managed by two females, was exquisitely clean from top to bottom.
Les Miserables	this was the only luxury the bishop allowed himself, for, as he said, "it takes nothing from the poor."
Les Miserables	we must allow, however, that of the old property there still remained six silver spoons and forks and a soup-ladle, which madame magloire daily saw with delight shining splendidly on the coarse white table-cloth.
Les Miserables	and as we are here depicting the bishop of d---- as he was, we must add that he had said, more than once, "i do not think i could give up eating with silver."
Les Miserables	to this plate must be added two heavy candlesticks of massive silver, which the bishop inherited from a great-aunt.
Les Miserables	these branched candlesticks each held two wax candles, and usually figured on the bishop's chimney.
Les Miserables	when he had any one to dinner, madame magloire lit the candles and placed the two candlesticks on the table.
Les Miserables	there was in the bishop's bed-room, at the head of his bed, a small cupboard in the wall, in which madame magloire each night placed the plate and the large ladle.
Les Miserables	i am bound to add that the key was never taken out.
Les Miserables	the garden, spoiled to some extent by the ugly buildings to which we have referred, was composed of four walks, radiating round a cesspool; another walk ran all round the garden close to the surrounding white wall.
Les Miserables	between these walks were four box-bordered squares.
Les Miserables	in three of them madame magloire grew vegetables; in the fourth the bishop had placed flowers; here and there were a few fruit-trees.
Les Miserables	once madame magloire had said, with a sort of gentle malice, "monseigneur, although you turn everything to use, here is an unemployed plot.
Les Miserables	it would be better to have lettuces there than bouquets."
Les Miserables	"madame magloire," the bishop answered, "you are mistaken; the beautiful is as useful as the useful."
Les Miserables	he added, after a moment's silence, "more so, perhaps."
Les Miserables	this square, composed of three or four borders, occupied the bishop almost as much as his books did.
Les Miserables	he liked to spend an hour or two there, cutting, raking, and digging holes in which he placed seeds.
Les Miserables	he was not so hostile to insects as a gardener would have liked.
Les Miserables	however, he made no pretensions to botany; he was ignorant of groups and solidism; he did not make the slightest attempt to decide between tournefort and the natural method; he was not a partisan either of jussieu or linnæus.
Les Miserables	he did not study plants, but he loved flowers.
Les Miserables	he greatly respected the professors, but he respected the ignorant even more; and without ever failing in this respect, he watered his borders every summer evening with a green-painted tin pot.
Les Miserables	the house had not a single door that locked.
Les Miserables	the door of the dining-room, which, as we said, opened right on the cathedral square, had formerly been adorned with bolts and locks like a prison gate.
Les Miserables	the bishop had all this iron removed, and the door was only hasped either night or day: the first passer-by, no matter the hour, had only to push it.
Les Miserables	at the outset the two females had been greatly alarmed by this never-closed door; but the bishop said to them, "have bolts placed on the doors of your rooms if you like."
Les Miserables	in the end they shared his confidence, or at least affected to do so: madame magloire alone was from time to time alarmed.
Les Miserables	as regards the bishop, his idea is explained, or at least indicated, by these three lines, which he wrote on the margin of a bible: "this is the distinction: the physician's doors must never be closed, the priest's door must always be open."
Les Miserables	on another book, entitled "philosophy of medical science," he wrote this other note: "am i not a physician like them?
Les Miserables	i also have my patients: in the first place, i have theirs, whom they call the sick, and then i have my own, whom i call the unhappy."
Les Miserables	elsewhere he also wrote: "do not ask the name of the man who seeks a bed from you, for it is before all the man whom his name embarrasses that needs an asylum."
Les Miserables	it came about that a worthy curé--i forget whether it were he of couloubroux or he of pompierry--thought proper to ask him one day, probably at the instigation of madame magloire, whether monseigneur was quite certain that he was not acting to some extent imprudently by leaving his door open day and night for any who liked to enter, and if he did not fear lest some misfortune might happen in a house so poorly guarded.
Les Miserables	the bishop tapped his shoulder with gentle gravity, and said to him, "nisi dominus custodierit domum, in vanum vigilant qui custodiunt eam."
Les Miserables	then he spoke of something else.
Les Miserables	he was fond of saying too, "there is the priest's bravery as well as that of the colonel of dragoons.
Les Miserables	the only thing is that ours must be quiet."
Les Miserables	chapter vii.
Les Miserables	cravatte.
Les Miserables	here naturally comes a fact which we must not omit, for it is one of those which will enable us to see what manner of man the bishop of d---- was.
Les Miserables	after the destruction of the band of gaspard bès, which had infested the gorges of ollioules, cravatte, one of his lieutenants, took refuge in the mountains.
Les Miserables	he concealed himself for a while with his brigands, the remnant of bès' band, in the county of nice, then went to piedmont, and suddenly re-appeared in france, via barcelonnette.
Les Miserables	he was seen first at jauziers, and next at tuiles; he concealed himself in the caverns of the joug de l'aigle, and descended thence on the hamlets and villages by the ravines of the ubaye.
Les Miserables	he pushed on even as far as embrun, entered the church one night and plundered the sacristy.
Les Miserables	his brigandage desolated the country, and the gendarmes were in vain placed on his track.
Les Miserables	he constantly escaped, and at times even offered resistance, for he was a bold scoundrel.
Les Miserables	in the midst of all this terror the bishop arrived on his visitation, and the mayor came to him and urged him to turn back.
Les Miserables	cravatte held the mountain as far as arche and beyond, and there was danger, even with an escort.
Les Miserables	it would be uselessly exposing three or four unhappy gendarmes.
Les Miserables	"for that reason," said the bishop, "i intend to go without escort."
Les Miserables	"can you mean it, monseigneur?"
Les Miserables	the mayor exclaimed.
Les Miserables	"i mean it so fully that i absolutely refuse gendarmes, and intend to start in an hour."
Les Miserables	"monseigneur, you will not do that!"
Les Miserables	"there is in the mountain," the bishop continued, "a humble little parish, which i have not visited for three years.
Les Miserables	they are good friends of mine, and quiet and honest shepherds.
Les Miserables	they are the owners of one goat out of every thirty they guard; they make very pretty woollen ropes of different colors, and they play mountain airs on small six-holed flutes.
Les Miserables	they want to hear about heaven every now and then, and what would they think of a bishop who was afraid?
Les Miserables	what would they say if i did not go?"
Les Miserables	"but, monseigneur, the brigands."
Les Miserables	"ah," said the bishop, "you are right; i may meet them.
Les Miserables	they too must want to hear about heaven."
Les Miserables	"but this band is a flock of wolves."
Les Miserables	"monsieur mayor, it may be that this is precisely the flock of which christ has made me the shepherd.
Les Miserables	who knows the ways of providence?"
Les Miserables	"monseigneur, they will plunder you."
Les Miserables	"i have nothing."
Les Miserables	"they will kill you."
Les Miserables	"a poor old priest who passes by, muttering his mummery?
Les Miserables	nonsense, what good would that do them?"
Les Miserables	"oh, good gracious, if you were to meet them!"
Les Miserables	"i would ask them for alms for my poor."
Les Miserables	"monseigneur, do not go.
Les Miserables	in heaven's name do not, for you expose your life."
Les Miserables	"my good sir," said the bishop, "is that all?
Les Miserables	i am not in this world to save my life, but to save souls."
Les Miserables	there was no help for it, and he set out only accompanied by a lad, who offered to act as his guide.
Les Miserables	his obstinacy created a sensation in the country, and caused considerable alarm.
Les Miserables	he would not take either his sister or madame magloire with him.
Les Miserables	he crossed the mountain on a mule, met nobody, and reached his good friends the goat-herds safe and sound.
Les Miserables	he remained with them a fortnight, preaching, administering the sacraments, teaching, and moralizing.
Les Miserables	when he was ready to start for home he resolved to sing a te deum pontifically, and spoke about it to the curé.
Les Miserables	but what was to be done?
Les Miserables	there were no episcopal ornaments.
Les Miserables	all that could be placed at his disposal was a poor village sacristy, with a few old faded and pinchbeck covered chasubles.
Les Miserables	"pooh!"
Les Miserables	said the bishop; "announce the te deum in your sermon for all that.
Les Miserables	it will come right in the end."
Les Miserables	inquiries were made in the surrounding churches: but all the magnificence of these united humble parishes would not have been sufficient decently to equip a cathedral chorister.
Les Miserables	while they were in this embarrassment a large chest was brought and left at the curacy for the bishop by two strange horse-men, who started again at once.
Les Miserables	the chest was opened and found to contain a cope of cloth of gold, a mitre adorned with diamonds, an archiepiscopal cross, a magnificent crozier, and all the pontifical robes stolen a month back from the treasury of our lady of embrun.
Les Miserables	in the chest was a paper on which were written these words: "cravatte to monseigneur welcome."
Les Miserables	"did i not tell you that it would be all right?"
Les Miserables	the bishop said; then he added with a smile, "god sends an archbishop's cope to a man who is contented with a curé's surplice."
Les Miserables	"monseigneur," the curé muttered, with a gentle shake of his head, "god--or the devil."
Les Miserables	the bishop looked fixedly at the curé and repeated authoritatively, "god!"
Les Miserables	when he returned to chastelon, and all along the road, he was regarded curiously.
Les Miserables	he found at the presbytery of that town mlle.
Les Miserables	baptistine and madame magloire waiting for him, and he said to his sister, "well, was i right?
Les Miserables	the poor priest went among these poor mountaineers with empty hands, and returns with his hands full.
Les Miserables	i started only taking with me my confidence in heaven, and i bring back the treasures of a cathedral."
Les Miserables	the same evening before retiring he said too, "never let us fear robbers or murderers.
Les Miserables	these are external and small dangers; let us fear ourselves; prejudices are the real robbers, vices the true murderers.
Les Miserables	the great dangers are within ourselves.
Les Miserables	let us not trouble about what threatens our head or purse, and only think of what threatens our soul."
Les Miserables	then, turning to his sister, he added, "sister, a priest ought never to take precautions against his neighbor.
Les Miserables	what his neighbor does god permits, so let us confine ourselves to praying to god when we believe that a danger is impending over us.
Les Miserables	let us pray, not for ourselves, but that our brother may not fall into error on our account."
Les Miserables	events, however, were rare in his existence.
Les Miserables	we relate those we know, but ordinarily he spent his life in always doing the same things at the same moment.
Les Miserables	a month of his year resembled an hour of his day.
Les Miserables	as to what became of the treasure of embrun cathedral, we should be greatly embarrassed if questioned on that head.
Les Miserables	there were many fine things, very tempting and famous to steal on behalf of the poor.
Les Miserables	stolen they were already, one moiety of the adventure was accomplished: the only thing left to do was to change the direction of the robbery, and make it turn slightly towards the poor.
Les Miserables	still, we affirm nothing on the subject; we merely mention that among the bishop's papers a rather obscure note was found, which probably refers to this question, and was thus conceived: "the question is to know whether it ought to go to the cathedral or the hospital."
Les Miserables	chapter viii.
Les Miserables	philosophy after drinking.
Les Miserables	the senator, to whom we have already alluded, was a skilful man, who had made his way with a rectitude that paid no attention to all those things which constitute obstacles, and are called conscience, plighted word, right, and duty: he had gone straight to his object without once swerving from the line of his promotions and his interest.
Les Miserables	he was an ex-procureur, softened by success, anything but a wicked man, doing all the little services in his power for his sons, his sons-in-law, his relatives, and even his friends: he had selected the best opportunities, and the rest seemed to him something absurd.
Les Miserables	he was witty, and just sufficiently lettered to believe himself a disciple of epicurus, while probably only a product of pigault lebrun.
Les Miserables	he was fond of laughing pleasantly at things infinite and eternal, and at the crotchets "of our worthy bishop."
Les Miserables	he even laughed at them with amiable authority in m. myriel's presence.
Les Miserables	on some semi-official occasion the count--(this senator) and m. myriel met at the prefect's table.
Les Miserables	at the dessert the senator, who was merry but quite sober, said,--  "come, bishop, let us have a chat.
Les Miserables	a senator and a bishop can hardly meet without winking at each other, for we are two augurs, and i am about to make a confession to you.
Les Miserables	i have my system of philosophy."
Les Miserables	"and you are right," the bishop answered; "as you make your philosophy, so you must lie on it.
Les Miserables	you are on the bed of purple."
Les Miserables	the senator, thus encouraged, continued,--"let us be candid."
Les Miserables	"decidedly."
Les Miserables	"i declare to you," the senator went on, "that the marquis d'argens, pyrrho, hobbes, and naigeon are no impostors.
Les Miserables	i have in my library all my philosophers with gilt backs."
Les Miserables	"like yourself, count," the bishop interrupted him.
Les Miserables	the senator proceeded,--  "i hate diderot; he is an ideologist, a declaimer, and a revolutionist, believing in his heart in deity, and more bigoted than voltaire.
Les Miserables	the latter ridiculed needham, and was wrong, for needham's eels prove that god is unnecessary.
Les Miserables	a drop of vinegar in a spoonful of flour supplies the _fiat lux_; suppose the drop larger, and the spoonful bigger, and you have the world.
Les Miserables	man is the eel; then, of what use is the eternal father?
Les Miserables	my dear bishop, the jehovah hypothesis wearies me; it is only fitted to produce thin people who think hollow.
Les Miserables	down with the great all which annoys me!
Les Miserables	long live zero, who leaves me at peace!
Les Miserables	between ourselves, and in order to confess to my pastor, as is right and proper, i confess to you that i possess common sense.
Les Miserables	i am not wild about your saviour, who continually preaches abnegation and sacrifice.
Les Miserables	it is advice offered by a miser to beggars.
Les Miserables	abnegation, why?
Les Miserables	sacrifice, for what object?
Les Miserables	i do not see that one wolf sacrifices itself to cause the happiness of another wolf.
Les Miserables	let us, therefore, remain in nature.
Les Miserables	we are at the summit, so let us have the supreme philosophy.
Les Miserables	what is the use of being at the top, if you cannot see further than the end of other people's noses?
Les Miserables	let us live gayly, for life is all in all.
Les Miserables	as for man having a future elsewhere, up there, down there, somewhere, i do not believe a syllable of it.
Les Miserables	oh yes!
Les Miserables	recommend sacrifices and abnegation to me.
Les Miserables	i must take care of all i do.
Les Miserables	i must rack my brains about good and evil, justice and injustice, fas et nefas.
Les Miserables	why so?
Les Miserables	because i shall have to give account for my actions.
Les Miserables	when?
Les Miserables	after my death.
Les Miserables	what a fine dream!
Les Miserables	after death!
Les Miserables	he will be a clever fellow who catches me.
Les Miserables	just think of a lump of ashes seized by a shadowy hand.
Les Miserables	let us speak the truth, we who are initiated and have raised the skirt of isis; there is no good, no evil, but there is vegetation.
Les Miserables	let us seek reality and go to the bottom; hang it all, we must scent the truth, dig into the ground for it and seize it.
Les Miserables	then it offers you exquisite delights; then you become strong and laugh.
Les Miserables	i am square at the base, my dear bishop, and human immortality is a thing which anybody who likes may listen to.
Les Miserables	oh!
Les Miserables	what a charming prospect!
Les Miserables	what a fine billet adam has!
Les Miserables	you are a soul, you will be an angel, and have blue wings on your shoulder-blades.
Les Miserables	come, help me, is it not tertullian who says that the blessed will go from one planet to the other?
Les Miserables	very good; they will be the grasshoppers of the planets.
Les Miserables	and then they will see god; ta, ta, ta.
Les Miserables	these paradises are all nonsense, and god is a monstrous fable.
Les Miserables	i would not say so in the _moniteur_, of course, but i whisper it between friends, _inter pocula_.
Les Miserables	sacrificing the earth for paradise is giving up the substance for the shadow.
Les Miserables	i am not such an ass as to be the dupe of the infinite.
Les Miserables	i am nothing, my name is count nothing, senator.
Les Miserables	did i exist before my birth?
Les Miserables	no; shall i exist after my death?
Les Miserables	no.
Les Miserables	what am i?
Les Miserables	a little dust aggregated by an organism.
Les Miserables	what have i to do on this earth?
Les Miserables	i have the choice between suffering and enjoyment.
Les Miserables	to what will suffering lead me?
Les Miserables	to nothingness, but i shall have suffered.
Les Miserables	to what will enjoyment lead me?
Les Miserables	to nothingness, but i shall have enjoyed.
Les Miserables	my choice is made; a man must either eat or be eaten, and so i eat, for it is better to be the tooth than the grass.
Les Miserables	that is my wisdom; after which go on as i impel you; the grave-digger is there, the pantheon for such as us, and all fall into the large hole.
Les Miserables	_finis_, and total liquidation, that is the vanishing point death is dead, take my word for it; and i laugh at the idea of any one present affirming the contrary.
Les Miserables	it is an invention of nurses, old bogey for children, jehovah for men.
Les Miserables	no, our morrow is night; behind the tomb there is nothing but equal nothings.
Les Miserables	you may have been sardanapalus, you may have been st. vincent de paul: it all comes to the same--nothing.
Les Miserables	that is the truth, so live above all else; make use of your _me_, so long as you hold it.
Les Miserables	in truth, i tell you, my dear bishop, i have my philosophy, and i have my philosophers, and i do not let myself be deluded by fables.
Les Miserables	after all, something must be offered persons who are down in the world,--the barefooted, the strugglers for existence and the wretched: and so they are offered pure legends--chimeras--the soul--immortality--paradise--the stars--to swallow.
Les Miserables	they chew that and put it on their dry bread.
Les Miserables	the man who has nothing has god, and that is something at any rate.
Les Miserables	i do not oppose it, but i keep m. naigeon for myself; god is good for the plebs."
Les Miserables	the bishop clapped his hands.
Les Miserables	"that is what i call speaking," he exclaimed.
Les Miserables	"ah, what an excellent and truly wonderful thing this materialism is!
Les Miserables	it is not every man who wishes that can have it.
Les Miserables	ah!
Les Miserables	when a man has reached that point, he is no longer a dupe; he does not let himself be stupidly exiled, like cato; or stoned, like st. stephen; or burnt, like joan of arc.
Les Miserables	those who have succeeded in acquiring this materialism have the joy of feeling themselves irresponsible, and thinking that they can devour everything without anxiety, places, sinecures, power well or badly gained, dignities, lucrative tergiversations, useful treachery, folly, capitulations with their consciences, and that they will go down to the tomb after digesting it all properly.
Les Miserables	how agreeable this is!
Les Miserables	i am not referring to you, my dear senator, still i cannot refrain from congratulating you.
Les Miserables	you great gentlemen have, as you say, a philosophy of your own, and for yourselves, exquisite, refined, accessible to the rich alone, good with any sauce, and admirably seasoning the joys of life.
Les Miserables	this philosophy is drawn from the profundities, and dug up by special searchers.
Les Miserables	but you are kind fellows, and think it no harm that belief in god should be the philosophy of the populace, much in the same way as a goose stuffed with chestnuts is the truffled turkey of the poor."
Les Miserables	chapter ix.
Les Miserables	the brother described by the sister.
Les Miserables	to give an idea of the domestic life of the bishop of d----, and the manner in which these two saintly women subordinated their actions, their thoughts, even their feminine instincts, which were easily startled, to the habits and intentions of the bishop, before he required to express them in words, we cannot do better than copy here a letter from mlle baptistine to the viscountess de boischevron, her friend of childhood.
Les Miserables	this letter is in our possession.
Les Miserables	"d----, 16th dec., 18----.
Les Miserables	"my dear madame,--not a day passes in which we do not talk about you.
Les Miserables	that is our general habit, but there is an extra reason at present.
Les Miserables	just imagine that, in washing and dusting the ceilings and walls, madame magloire has made a discovery, and now our two rooms papered with old white-washed paper would not disgrace a chateau like yours.
Les Miserables	madame magloire has torn down all the paper, and there are things under it.
Les Miserables	my sitting-room, in which there was no furniture, and in which we used to hang up the linen to dry, is fifteen feet in height, eighteen wide, and has a ceiling which was once gilded, and rafters, as in your house.
Les Miserables	it was covered with canvas during the time this mansion was an hospital.
Les Miserables	but it is my bed-room, you should see; madame magloire has discovered, under at least ten layers of paper, paintings which, though not excellent, are endurable.
Les Miserables	there is telemachus dubbed a knight by minerva; and there he is again in the gardens: i forget their names, but where the roman ladies only went for a single night.
Les Miserables	what can i tell you?
Les Miserables	i have roman ladies (_here an illegible word_), and so on.
Les Miserables	madame magloire has got it all straight.
Les Miserables	this summer she intends to repair a little damage, re-varnish it all, and my bed-room will be a real museum.
Les Miserables	she has also found in a corner of the garret two consoles in the old fashion; they want twelve francs to regild them, but it is better to give that sum to the poor: besides, they are frightfully ugly, and i should prefer a round mahogany table.
Les Miserables	"i am very happy, for my brother is so good; he gives all he has to the sick and the poor, and we are often greatly pressed.
Les Miserables	the country is hard in winter, and something must be done for those who are in want.
Les Miserables	we are almost lighted and warmed, and, as you can see, that is a great comfort.
Les Miserables	my brother has peculiar habits; when he does talk, he says 'that a bishop should be so.'
Les Miserables	just imagine that the house door is never closed: any one who likes can come in, and is at once in my brother's presence.
Les Miserables	he fears nothing, not even night; and he says that is his way of showing his bravery.
Les Miserables	he does not wish me to feel alarmed for him, or for madame magloire to do so; he exposes himself to all dangers, and does not wish us to appear as if we even noticed it.
Les Miserables	we must understand him.
Les Miserables	he goes out in the rain, he wades through the water, and travels in winter.
Les Miserables	he is not afraid of the night, suspicious roads, or encounters.
Les Miserables	last year he went all alone into a country of robbers, for he would not take us with him.
Les Miserables	he stayed away a whole fortnight, and folk thought him dead, but he came back all right, and said, 'here's the way in which i was robbed,' and he opened a chest full of all the treasures of embrun cathedral, which the robbers had given him.
Les Miserables	that time i could not refrain from scolding him a little, but was careful only to speak when the wheels made a noise, so that no one could hear me.
Les Miserables	"at first i said to myself; there is no danger that checks him, and he is terrible; but at present i have grown accustomed to it.
Les Miserables	i make madame magloire a sign not to annoy him, and he risks his life as he pleases.
Les Miserables	i carry off magloire, go to my bed-room, pray for him, and fall asleep.
Les Miserables	i am tranquil because i know that if any harm happened to him it would be the death of me.
Les Miserables	i shall go to heaven with my brother and my bishop.
