Les Miserables	after examining the man for some minutes as if he had been a viper, the peasant returned to the door and said: "be off!"
Les Miserables	"for mercy's sake," the man continued,--"a glass of water."
Les Miserables	"a charge of shot!"
Les Miserables	the peasant said.
Les Miserables	then he violently closed the door, and the stranger heard two bolts fastened.
Les Miserables	a moment after the window shutters were closed, and the sound of the iron bar being put in reached his ear.
Les Miserables	night was coming on apace: the cold wind of the alps was blowing.
Les Miserables	by the light of the expiring day the stranger noticed in one of the gardens a sort of hut which seemed to him to be made of sods of turf.
Les Miserables	he boldly clambered over a railing and found himself in the garden; he approached the hut, which had as entrance a narrow, extremely low door, and resembled the tenements which road-menders construct by the side of the highway.
Les Miserables	he doubtless thought it was such: he was suffering from cold and hunger, and though he had made up his mind to starve, it was at any rate a shelter against the cold.
Les Miserables	as this sort of residence is not usually occupied at night, he lay down on his stomach and crawled into the hut: it was warm, and he found a rather good straw litter in it.
Les Miserables	he lay for a moment motionless on this bed as his fatigue was so great: but as his knapsack hurt his back and was a ready-made pillow, he began unbuckling one of the thongs.
Les Miserables	at this moment a hoarse growl was audible: he raised his eyes, and the head of an enormous mastiff stood out in the shadow at the opening of the hut, which was its kennel.
Les Miserables	the dog itself was strong and formidable, hence he raised his stick, employed his knapsack as a shield, and left the kennel as he best could, though not without enlarging the rents in his rags.
Les Miserables	he also left the garden, but backwards, and compelled to twirl his stick in order to keep the dog at a respectful distance.
Les Miserables	when he, not without difficulty, had leaped the fence again, and found himself once more in the street, alone, without a bed, roof, or shelter, and expelled even from the bed of straw and the kennel, he fell rather than sat on a stone, and a passer-by heard him exclaim, "i am not even a dog."
Les Miserables	he soon rose and recommenced his walk.
Les Miserables	he left the town hoping to find some tree or mill in the fields which would afford him shelter.
Les Miserables	he walked on thus for some time with hanging head; when he found himself far from all human habitations, he raised his eyes and looked around him.
Les Miserables	he was in a field, and had in front of him one of those low hills with close-cut stubble, which after harvest resemble cropped heads.
Les Miserables	the horizon was perfectly black, but it was not solely the gloom of night, but low clouds, which seemed to be resting on the hill itself, rose and filled the whole sky.
Les Miserables	still, as the moon was about to rise shortly, and a remnant of twilight still hovered in the zenith, these clouds formed a species of whitish vault whence a gleam of light was thrown on the earth.
Les Miserables	the ground was therefore more illumined than the sky, which produces a peculiarly sinister effect, and the hill with its paltry outlines stood out vaguely and dully on the gloomy horizon.
Les Miserables	the whole scene was hideous, mean, mournful, and confined; there was nothing in the field or on the hill but a stunted tree, which writhed and trembled a few yards from the traveller.
Les Miserables	this man was evidently far from possessing those delicate habits of mind which render persons sensible of the mysterious aspects of things, still there was in the sky, this hill, this plain, and this tree, something so profoundly desolate, that after standing motionless and thoughtful for a while he suddenly turned back.
Les Miserables	there are instants in which nature seems to be hostile.
Les Miserables	he went back and found the gates of the town closed.
Les Miserables	d----, which sustained sieges in the religious wars, was still begirt in 1815 by old walls flanked by square towers, which have since been demolished.
Les Miserables	he passed through a breach, and re-entered the town.
Les Miserables	it might be about eight o'clock in the evening, and as he did not know the streets he wandered about without purpose.
Les Miserables	he thus reached the prefecture and then the seminary; on passing through the cathedral square he shook his fist at the church.
Les Miserables	there is at the corner of this square a printing-office, where the proclamations of the emperor and the imperial guard to the army, brought from elba, and drawn up by napoleon himself, were first printed.
Les Miserables	worn out with fatigue, and hopeless, he sat down on the stone bench at the door of this printing-office.
Les Miserables	an old lady who was leaving the church at the moment saw the man stretched out in the darkness.
Les Miserables	"what are you doing there, my friend?"
Les Miserables	she said.
Les Miserables	he answered, harshly and savagely, "you can see, my good woman, that i am going to sleep."
Les Miserables	the good woman, who was really worthy of the name, was the marchioness de r----.
Les Miserables	"on that bench?"
Les Miserables	she continued.
Les Miserables	"i have had for nineteen years a wooden mattress," the man said, "and now i have a stone one."
Les Miserables	"have you been a soldier?"
Les Miserables	"yes, my good woman."
Les Miserables	"why do you not go to the inn?"
Les Miserables	"because i have no money."
Les Miserables	"alas!"
Les Miserables	said madame de r----, "i have only two-pence in my purse."
Les Miserables	"you can give them to me all the same."
Les Miserables	the man took the money, and madame de r---- continued, "you cannot lodge at an inn for so small a sum, still you should make the attempt, for you cannot possibly spend the night here.
Les Miserables	doubtless you are cold and hungry, and some one might take you in for charity."
Les Miserables	"i have knocked at every door."
Les Miserables	"well?"
Les Miserables	"and was turned away at all."
Les Miserables	the "good woman" touched the man's arm and pointed to a small house next to the bishop's palace.
Les Miserables	"you have," she continued, "knocked at every door.
Les Miserables	have you done so there?"
Les Miserables	"no."
Les Miserables	"then do it."
Les Miserables	chapter ii   prudence recommended to wisdom.
Les Miserables	on this evening, the bishop of d----, after his walk in the town, had remained in his bed-room till a late hour.
Les Miserables	he was engaged on a heavy work on the "duties," which he unfortunately has left incomplete.
Les Miserables	he was still working at eight o'clock, writing rather uncomfortably on small squares of paper, with a large book open on his knees, when madame magloire came in as usual to fetch the plate from the wall-cupboard near the bed.
Les Miserables	a moment after, the bishop, feeling that supper was ready, and that his sister might be waiting, closed his book, rose from the table, and walked into the dining-room.
Les Miserables	it was an oblong apartment, as we have said, with a door opening on the street, and a window looking on the garden.
Les Miserables	madame magloire had laid the table, and while attending to her duties, was chatting with mademoiselle baptistine.
Les Miserables	a lamp was on the table, which was close to the chimney, in which a tolerable fire was lighted.
Les Miserables	we can easily figure to ourselves the two females, who had both passed their sixtieth year: madame magloire, short, stout, and quick: mademoiselle baptistine, gentle, thin, and frail, somewhat taller than her brother, dressed in a puce-colored silk gown, the fashionable color in 1806, which she had bought in paris in that year and which still held out.
Les Miserables	madame magloire wore a white cap, on her neck a gold _jeannette,_ the only piece of feminine jewelry in the house, a very white handkerchief emerging from a black stuff gown with wide and short sleeves, a calico red and puce checked apron, fastened round the waist with a green ribbon, with a stomacher of the same stuff fastened with two pins at the top corners, heavy shoes and yellow stockings, like the marseilles women.
Les Miserables	mademoiselle baptistine's gown was cut after the fashion of 1806, short-waisted, with epaulettes on the sleeves, flaps and buttons, and she concealed her gray hair by a curling front called _à l'enfant_.
Les Miserables	madame magloire had an intelligent, quick, and kindly air, though the unevenly raised corners of her mouth and the upper lip, thicker than the lower, gave her a somewhat rough and imperious air.
Les Miserables	so long as monseigneur was silent, she spoke to him boldly with a mingled respect and liberty, but so soon as he spoke she passively obeyed, like mademoiselle, who no longer replied, but restricted herself to obeying and enduring.
Les Miserables	even when she was young the latter was not pretty; she had large blue eyes, flush with her head, and a long peaked nose; but all her face, all her person, as we said at the outset, breathed ineffable kindness.
Les Miserables	she had always been predestined to gentleness, but faith, hope, and charity, those three virtues that softly warm the soul, had gradually elevated that gentleness to sanctity.
Les Miserables	nature had only made her a lamb, and religion had made her an angel.
Les Miserables	poor holy woman!
Les Miserables	sweet departed recollection!
Les Miserables	mademoiselle afterwards narrated so many times what took place at the bishopric on this evening that several persons still living remember the slightest details.
Les Miserables	at the moment when the bishop entered madame magloire was talking with some vivacity; she was conversing with mademoiselle on a subject that was familiar to her, and to which the bishop was accustomed--it was the matter of the frontdoor latch.
Les Miserables	it appears that while going to purchase something for supper, madame magloire had heard things spoken of in certain quarters; people were talking of an ill-looking prowler, that a suspicious vagabond had arrived, who must be somewhere in the town, and that it would possibly be an unpleasant thing for any one out late to meet him.
Les Miserables	the police were very badly managed because the prefect and the mayor were not friendly, and tried to injure each other by allowing things to happen.
Les Miserables	hence wise people would be their own police, and be careful to close their houses _and lock their doors._  madame magloire italicized the last sentence, but the bishop had come from his room where it was rather cold, and was warming himself at the fire while thinking of other matters; in fact, he did not pick up the words which madame magloire had just let drop.
Les Miserables	she repeated them, and then mademoiselle, who wished to satisfy madame magloire without displeasing her brother, ventured to say timidly,--  "brother, do you hear what madame magloire is saying?"
Les Miserables	"i vaguely heard something," the bishop answered; then he half turned his chair, placed his hand on his knees, and looked up at the old servant with his cordial and easily-pleased face, which the fire illumined from below: "well, what is it?
Les Miserables	what is it?
Les Miserables	are we in any great danger?"
Les Miserables	then madame magloire told her story over again, while exaggerating it slightly, though unsuspicious of the fact.
Les Miserables	it would seem that a gypsy, a barefooted fellow, a sort of dangerous beggar, was in the town at the moment.
Les Miserables	he had tried to get a lodging at jacquin labarre's, who had refused to take him in.
Les Miserables	he had been seen prowling about the streets at nightfall, and was evidently a gallows bird, with his frightful face.
Les Miserables	"is he really?"
Les Miserables	said the bishop.
Les Miserables	this cross-questioning encouraged madame magloire; it seemed to indicate that the bishop was beginning to grow alarmed, and hence she continued triumphantly,--  "yes, monseigneur, it is so, and some misfortune will occur in the town this night: everybody says so, and then the police are so badly managed [useful repetition].
Les Miserables	fancy living in a mountain town, and not even having lanterns in the streets at nights!
Les Miserables	you go out and find yourself in pitch darkness.
Les Miserables	i say, monseigneur, and mademoiselle says--"  "i," the sister interrupted, "say nothing; whatever my brother does is right."
Les Miserables	madame magloire continued, as if no protest had been made,--  "we say that this house is not at all safe, and that if monseigneur permits i will go to paulin musebois, the locksmith, and tell him to put the old bolts on the door again; i have them by me, and it will not take a minute; and i say, monseigneur, that we ought to have bolts if it were only for this night, for i say that a door which can be opened from the outside by the first passer-by is most terrible: besides, monseigneur is always accustomed to say "come in," and in the middle of the night, oh, my gracious!
Les Miserables	there is no occasion to ask for permission."
Les Miserables	at this moment there was a rather loud rap at the front door.
Les Miserables	"come in," said the bishop.
Les Miserables	chapter iii.
Les Miserables	the heroism of passive obedience.
Les Miserables	the door was thrown open wide, as if some one were pushing it energetically and resolutely.
Les Miserables	a man entered whom we already know; it was the traveller whom we saw just now wandering about in search of a shelter.
Les Miserables	he entered and stopped, leaving the door open behind him.
Les Miserables	he had his knapsack on his shoulder, his stick in his hand, and a rough, bold, wearied, and violent expression in his eyes.
Les Miserables	the fire-light fell on him; he was hideous; it was a sinister apparition.
Les Miserables	madame magloire had not even the strength to utter a cry, she shivered and stood with widely-open mouth.
Les Miserables	mademoiselle baptistine turned, perceived the man who entered, and half started up in terror; then, gradually turning her head to the chimney, she began looking at her brother, and her face became again calm and serene.
Les Miserables	the bishop fixed a quiet eye on the man, as he opened his mouth, doubtless to ask the new-comer what he wanted.
Les Miserables	the man leaned both his hands on his stick, looked in turn at the two aged females and the old man, and, not waiting for the bishop to speak, said in a loud voice,--  "look here!
Les Miserables	my name is jean valjean.
Les Miserables	i am a galley-slave, and have spent nineteen years in the bagne.
Les Miserables	i was liberated four days ago, and started for pontarlier, which is my destination.
Les Miserables	i have been walking for four days since i left toulon, and to-day i have marched twelve leagues.
Les Miserables	this evening on coming into the town i went to the inn, but was sent away in consequence of my yellow passport, which i had shown at the police office.
Les Miserables	i went to another inn, and the landlord said to me, "be off!"
Les Miserables	it was the same everywhere, and no one would have any dealings with me.
Les Miserables	i went to the prison, but the jailer would not take me in.
Les Miserables	i got into a dogs kennel, but the dog bit me and drove me off, as if it had been a man; it seemed to know who i was.
Les Miserables	i went into the fields to sleep in the star-light, but there were no stars.
Les Miserables	i thought it would rain, and as there was no god to prevent it from raining, i came back to the town to sleep in a doorway.
Les Miserables	i was lying down on a stone in the square, when a good woman pointed to your house, and said, "go and knock there."
Les Miserables	what sort of a house is this?
Les Miserables	do you keep an inn?
Les Miserables	i have money, 109 francs 15 sous, which i earned at the bagne by my nineteen years' toil.
Les Miserables	i will pay, for what do i care for that, as i have money!
Les Miserables	i am very tired and frightfully hungry; will you let me stay here?"
Les Miserables	"madame magloire," said the bishop, "you will lay another knife and fork."
Les Miserables	the man advanced three paces, and approached the lamp which was on the table.
Les Miserables	"wait a minute," he continued, as if he had not comprehended, "that will not do.
Les Miserables	did you not hear me say that i was a galley-slave, a convict, and have just come from the bagne?"
Les Miserables	he took from his pocket a large yellow paper, which he unfolded.
Les Miserables	"here is my passport, yellow as you see, which turns me out wherever i go.
Les Miserables	will you read it?
Les Miserables	i can read it, for i learned to do so at the bagne, where there is a school for those who like to attend it.
Les Miserables	this is what is written in my passport: 'jean valjean, a liberated convict, native of'--but that does not concern you--'has remained nineteen years at the galleys.
Les Miserables	five years for robbery with house-breaking, fourteen years for having tried to escape four times.
Les Miserables	the man is very dangerous.'
Les Miserables	all the world has turned me out, and are you willing to receive me?
Les Miserables	is this an inn?
Les Miserables	will you give me some food and a bed?
Les Miserables	have you a stable?"
Les Miserables	"madame magloire," said the bishop, "you will put clean sheets on the bed in the alcove."
Les Miserables	we have already explained of what nature was the obedience of the two females.
Les Miserables	madame magloire left the room to carry out the orders.
Les Miserables	the bishop turned to the man.
Les Miserables	"sit down and warm yourself, sir.
Les Miserables	we shall sup directly, and your bed will be got ready while we are supping."
Les Miserables	the man understood this at once.
Les Miserables	the expression of his face, which had hitherto been gloomy and harsh, was marked with stupefaction, joy, doubt, and became extraordinary.
Les Miserables	he began stammering like a lunatic.
Les Miserables	"is it true?

Les Miserables	you will let me stay, you will not turn me out, a convict?
Les Miserables	you call me _sir,_ you do not 'thou' me.
Les Miserables	'get out, dog!'
Les Miserables	that is what is always said to me; i really believed that you would turn me out, and hence told you at once who i am.
Les Miserables	oh!
Les Miserables	what a worthy woman she was who sent me here!
Les Miserables	i shall have supper, a bed with mattresses and sheets, like everybody else.
Les Miserables	for nineteen years i have not slept in a bed!

Les Miserables	he is the curé over the curés, you know.
Les Miserables	pardon, i express it badly; but it is so far above me, a poor convict, you see.

Les Miserables	he spoke, but was too far off, and we did not hear him.
Les Miserables	that is what a bishop is."
Les Miserables	while he was speaking the bishop had gone to close the door, which had been left open.

Les Miserables	each time he said the word _sir_ with his gentle grave voice the man's face was illumined.
Les Miserables	_sir_ to a convict is the glass of water to the shipwrecked sailor of the méduse.
Les Miserables	ignominy thirsts for respect.
Les Miserables	"this lamp gives a very bad light," the bishop continued.
Les Miserables	madame magloire understood, and fetched from the chimney of monseigneur's bed-room the two silver candlesticks, which she placed on the table ready lighted.
Les Miserables	"monsieur le curé," said the man, "you are good, and do not despise me.
Les Miserables	you receive me as a friend and light your wax candles for me, and yet i have not hidden from you whence i come, and that i am an unfortunate fellow."
Les Miserables	the bishop, who was seated by his side, gently touched his hand.
Les Miserables	"you need not have told me who you were; this is not my house, but the house of christ.
Les Miserables	this door does not ask a man who enters whether he has a name, but if he has a sorrow; you are suffering, you are hungry and thirsty, and so be welcome.
Les Miserables	and do not thank me, or say that i am receiving you in my house, for no one is at home here excepting the man who has need of an asylum.
Les Miserables	i tell you, who are a passer-by, that you are more at home here than i am myself, and all there is here is yours.
Les Miserables	why do i want to know your name?
Les Miserables	besides, before you told it to me you had one which i knew."
Les Miserables	the man opened his eyes in amazement.
Les Miserables	"is that true?
Les Miserables	you know my name?"
Les Miserables	"yes," the bishop answered, "you are my brother."
Les Miserables	"monsieur le curé," the man exclaimed, "i was very hungry when i came in, but you are so kind that i do not know at present what i feel; it has passed over."
Les Miserables	the bishop looked at him and said,--  "you have suffered greatly?"
Les Miserables	"oh!
Les Miserables	the red jacket, the cannon ball on your foot, a plank to sleep on, heat, cold, labor, the set of men, the blows, the double chain for a nothing, a dungeon for a word, even when you are ill in bed, and the chain-gang.
Les Miserables	the very dogs are happier.
Les Miserables	nineteen years!
Les Miserables	and now i am forty-six; and at present, the yellow passport!
Les Miserables	there it is!"
Les Miserables	"yes," said the bishop, "you have come from a place of sorrow.
Les Miserables	listen to me; there will be more joy in heaven over the tearful face of a repentant sinner than over the white robes of one hundred just men.
Les Miserables	if you leave that mournful place with thoughts of hatred and anger against your fellow-men you are worthy of pity; if you leave it with thoughts of kindliness, gentleness, and peace, you are worth more than any of us."
Les Miserables	in the meanwhile madame magloire had served the soup: it was made of water, oil, bread, and salt, and a little bacon, and the rest of the supper consisted of a piece of mutton, figs, a fresh cheese, and a loaf of rye bread.
Les Miserables	she had herself added a bottle of old mauves wine.
Les Miserables	the bishop's face suddenly assumed the expression of gayety peculiar to hospitable natures.
Les Miserables	"to table," he said eagerly, as he was wont to do when any stranger supped with him; and he bade the man sit down on his right hand, while mlle.
Les Miserables	baptistine, perfectly peaceful and natural, took her seat on his left.
Les Miserables	the bishop said grace, and then served the soup himself, according to his wont.
Les Miserables	the man began eating greedily.
Les Miserables	all at once the bishop said,--  "it strikes me that there is something wanting on the table."
Les Miserables	madame magloire, truth to tell, had only laid the absolutely necessary silver.
Les Miserables	now it was the custom in this house, when the bishop had any one to supper, to arrange the whole stock of plate on the table, as an innocent display.
Les Miserables	this graceful semblance of luxury was a species of childishness full of charm in this gentle and strict house, which elevated poverty to dignity.
Les Miserables	madame magloire took the hint, went out without a word, and a moment after the remaining spoons and forks glittered on the cloth, symmetrically arranged before each of the guests.
Les Miserables	chapter iv.
Les Miserables	cheesemaking at pontarlier.
Les Miserables	and now, in order to give an idea of what took place at table, we cannot do better than transcribe a passage of a letter written by mademoiselle baptistine to madame boischevron, in which the conversation between the convict and the bishop is recorded with simple minuteness.
Les Miserables	*       *       *       *       *  "the man paid no attention to any one; he ate with frightful voracity, but after supper he said,--  "monsieur le curé, all this is much too good for me; but i am bound to say that the carriers who would not let me sup with them have better cheer than you."
Les Miserables	"between ourselves, this remark slightly offended me, but my brother answered,--  "they are harder worked than i am."
Les Miserables	"no," the man continued, "they have more money.
Les Miserables	you are poor, as i can plainly see; perhaps you are not even curé.
Les Miserables	ah, if heaven were just you ought to be a curé."
Les Miserables	"heaven is more than just," said my brother.
Les Miserables	a moment after he added,--  "monsieur jean valjean, i think you said you were going to pontarlier?"
Les Miserables	"i am compelled to go there."
Les Miserables	then he continued, "i must be off by sunrise to-morrow morning; it is a tough journey, for if the nights are cold the days are hot."
Les Miserables	"you are going to an excellent part of the country," my brother resumed.
Les Miserables	"when the revolution ruined my family i sought shelter first in franche comté, and lived there for some time by the labor of my arms.
Les Miserables	i had a good will, and found plenty to do, as i need only choose.
Les Miserables	there are paper-mills, tanneries, distilleries, oil-mills, wholesale manufactories of clocks, steel works, copper works, and at least twenty iron foundries, of which the four at lods, chatillon, audincourt, and beure are very large."
Les Miserables	"i am pretty sure i am not mistaken, and that they are the names my brother mentioned; then he broke off and addressed me.
Les Miserables	"my dear sister, have we not some relatives in those parts?"
Les Miserables	"my answer was, 'we used to have some; among others monsieur de lucinet, who was captain of the gates at pontarlier, under the ancient régime."
Les Miserables	"yes," my brother continued, "but in '93 people had no relatives, but only their arms, and so i worked.
Les Miserables	in the country to which you are going, monsieur valjean, there is a truly patriarchal and pleasing trade.
Les Miserables	my dear sister, i mean their cheese manufactures, which they call _fruitières_."
Les Miserables	"then my brother, while pressing this man to eat, explained in their fullest details the _fruitières_ of pontarlier, which were divided into two classes--the large farms which belong to the rich, and where there are forty or fifty cows, which produce seven to eight thousand cheeses in the summer, and the partnership _fruitières_, which belong to the poor.
Les Miserables	the peasants of the central mountain district keep their cows in common and divide the produce.
Les Miserables	they have a cheese-maker, who is called the _grurin_; he receives the milk from the partners thrice a day, and enters the quantities in a book.
Les Miserables	the cheese-making begins about the middle of april, and the dairy farmers lead their cows to the mountains toward midsummer.
Les Miserables	"the man grew animated while eating, and my brother made him drink that excellent mauves wine, which he does not drink himself because he says that it is expensive.
Les Miserables	my brother gave him all these details with that easy gayety of his which you know, mingling his remarks with graceful appeals to myself.
Les Miserables	he dwelt a good deal on the comfortable position of the _grurin_, as if wishful that this man should understand, without advising him directly and harshly, that it would be a refuge for him.
Les Miserables	one thing struck me: the man was as i have described him to you; well, my brother, during the whole of supper, and indeed of the evening, did not utter a word which could remind this man of what he was, or tell him who my brother was.
Les Miserables	it was apparently a good opportunity to give him a little lecture, and let the bishop produce a permanent effect on the galley-slave.
Les Miserables	it might have seemed to any one else that having this wretched man in hand it would be right to feed his mind at the same time as his body, and address to him some reproaches seasoned with morality and advice, or at any rate a little commiseration, with an exhortation to behave better in future.
Les Miserables	my brother did not even ask him where he came from, or his history, for his fault is contained in his history, and my brother appeared to avoid everything which might call it to his mind.
Les Miserables	this was carried to such a point that at a certain moment, when my brother was talking about the mountaineers of pontarlier, 'who had a pleasant task near heaven,' and who, he added, 'are happy because they are innocent,' he stopped short, fearing lest there might be in the remark something which might unpleasantly affect this man.
Les Miserables	after considerable reflection, i believe i can understand what was going on in my brother's heart: he doubtless thought that this jean valjean had his misery ever present to his mind, that the best thing was to distract his attention, and make him believe, were it only momentarily, that he was a man like the rest, by behaving to him as he would to others.
Les Miserables	was not this really charity?
Les Miserables	is there not, my dear lady, something truly evangelical in this delicacy, which abstains from all lecturing and allusions, and is it not the best pity, when a man has a sore point, not to touch it at all?
Les Miserables	it seemed to me that this might be my brother's innermost thought: in any case, what i can safely say is, that if he had all these ideas, he did not let any of them be visible, even to me; he was from beginning to end the same man he is every night, and he supped with jean valjean with the same air and in the same way as if he had been supping with m. gedeon le prevost, or with the parish curate.
Les Miserables	"toward the end, when we had come to the figs, there was a knock at the door.
Les Miserables	it was mother gerbaud with her little baby in her arms.
Les Miserables	my brother kissed the child's forehead, and borrowed from me 15 sous which i happened to have about me, to give them to the mother.
Les Miserables	the man, while this was going on, did not seem to pay great attention: he said nothing, and seemed very tired.

Les Miserables	madame magloire hastily removed the plate.

Les Miserables	i, however, sent madame magloire to lay on the man's bed a roebuck's hide from the black forest, which was in my room, for the nights are very cold, and that keeps you wann.

Les Miserables	my brother bought it when he was in germany, at tottlingen, near the source of the danube, as well as the small ivory-handled knife which i use at meals.
Les Miserables	"madame magloire came up again almost immediately.

Les Miserables	chapter v.   tranquillity.

Les Miserables	the man followed him.
Les Miserables	the reader will remember, from our description, that the rooms were so arranged that in order to reach the oratory where the alcove was it was necessary to pass through the bishop's bed-room.
Les Miserables	at the moment when he went through this room madame magloire was putting away the plate in the cupboard over the bed-head: it was the last job she did every night before retiring.

Les Miserables	then gravely moving his lips, like a man who is praying and speaking to himself, he stretched out two fingers of his right hand and blessed the man, who did not bow his head, and returned to his bed-room, without turning his head or looking behind him.
Les Miserables	when the alcove was occupied, a large serge curtain drawn right across the oratory concealed the altar.
Les Miserables	the bishop knelt down as he passed before this curtain, and offered up a short prayer; a moment after he was in his garden, walking, dreaming, contemplating, his soul and thoughts entirely occupied by those grand mysteries which god displays at night to eyes that remain open.
Les Miserables	as for the man, he was really so wearied that he did not even take advantage of the nice white sheets.
