Les Miserables	the persistency of the public prosecutor was visibly in contradiction with the feelings of all,--the public, the court, and the jury.
Les Miserables	the counsel for the defence had little difficulty in refuting his arguments, and establishing that through the revelations of m. madeleine, that is to say, the real jean valjean, circumstances were entirely altered, and the jury had an innocent man before them.
Les Miserables	the barrister deduced a few arguments, unfortunately rather stale, about judicial errors, etc., the president in his summing-up supported the defence, and the jury in a few moments acquitted champmathieu.
Les Miserables	still, the public prosecutor wanted a jean valjean; and, as he no longer had champmathieu, he took madeleine.
Les Miserables	immediately after champmathieu was acquitted, he had a conference with the president as to the necessity of seizing the person of the mayor of m----, and after the first emotion had passed, the president raised but few objections.
Les Miserables	justice must take its course; and then, to tell the whole truth, although the president was a kind and rather sensible man, he was at the same time a very ardent royalist, and had been offended by the way in which the mayor of m----, in alluding to the landing at cannes, employed the words "the emperor" and not "buonaparte."
Les Miserables	the order of arrest was consequently made out, and the prosecutor at once sent it off by express to m----, addressed to inspector javert, who, as we know, returned home immediately after he had given his evidence.
Les Miserables	javert was getting up at the moment when the messenger handed him the order of arrest and the warrant.
Les Miserables	this messenger was himself a very skilful policeman, who informed javert in two words of what had occurred at arras.
Les Miserables	the order of arrest, signed by the public prosecutor, was thus conceived: "inspector javert will apprehend monsieur madeleine, mayor of m----, who in this day's session was recognized as the liberated convict, jean valjean."
Les Miserables	any one who did not know javert and had seen him at the moment when he entered the infirmary ante-room, could not have guessed what was taking place, but would have considered him to be as usual.
Les Miserables	he was cold, calm, serious, his gray hair was smoothed down on his temples, and he went up the stairs with his usual slowness.
Les Miserables	but any one who was well acquainted with him, and examined him closely, would have shuddered; the buckle of his leathern stock, instead of sitting in the nape of his neck, was under his left ear.
Les Miserables	this revealed an extraordinary agitation.
Les Miserables	javert was a complete character, without a crease in his duty or in his uniform: methodical with criminals, and rigid with his coat-buttons.
Les Miserables	for him to have his stock out of order, it was necessary for him to be suffering from one of those emotions which might be called internal earthquakes.
Les Miserables	he had merely fetched a corporal and four men from the guardhouse close by, left them in the yard, and had fantine's room pointed out to him by the unsuspecting portress, who was accustomed to see policemen ask for the mayor.
Les Miserables	on reaching fantine's door, javert turned the key, pushed the door with the gentleness either of a sick-nurse or a spy, and entered.
Les Miserables	correctly speaking, he did not enter: he stood in the half-opened door with his hat on his head, and his left hand thrust into the breast of his great-coat, which was buttoned to the chin.
Les Miserables	under his elbow could be seen the leaden knob of his enormous cane, which was concealed behind his back.
Les Miserables	he remained thus for many a minute, no one perceiving his presence.
Les Miserables	all at once fantine raised her eyes, saw him, and made m. madeleine turn.
Les Miserables	at the moment when madeleine's glance met javert's, the latter, without stirring or drawing near, became fearful.
Les Miserables	no human feeling can succeed in being so horrible as joy.
Les Miserables	it was the face of a fiend who has just found a condemned soul again.
Les Miserables	the certainty of at length holding jean valjean caused all he had in his soul to appear on his countenance, and the stirred-up sediment rose to the surface.
Les Miserables	the humiliation of having lost the trail for a while and having been mistaken with regard to champmathieu was effaced by his pride at having guessed so correctly at the beginning, and having a right instinct for such a length of time.
Les Miserables	javert's satisfaction was displayed in his sovereign attitude, and the deformity of triumph was spread over his narrow forehead.
Les Miserables	javert at this moment was in heaven: without distinctly comprehending the fact, but still with a confused intuition of his necessity and his success, he, javert, personified justice, light, and truth in their celestial function of crushing evil.
Les Miserables	he had behind him, around him, at an infinite depth, authority, reason, the legal conscience, the public vindication, all the stars: he protected order, he drew the lightning from the law, he avenged society, he rendered assistance to the absolute.
Les Miserables	there was in his victory a remnant of defiance and contest: upright, haughty, and dazzling, he displayed the superhuman bestiality of a ferocious archangel in the bright azure of heaven.
Les Miserables	the formidable shadow of the deed he was doing rendered visible to his clutching fist the flashing social sword.
Les Miserables	happy and indignant, he held beneath his heel, crime, vice, perdition, rebellion, and hell: he was radiant, he exterminated, he smiled, and there was an incontestable grandeur in this monstrous st. michael.
Les Miserables	javert, though terrifying, was not ignoble.
Les Miserables	probity, sincerity, candor, conviction, and the idea of duty, are things which, by deceiving themselves, may become hideous, but which, even if hideous, remain grand; their majesty, peculiar to the human conscience, persists in horror; they are virtues which have but one vice, error.
Les Miserables	the pitiless honest joy of a fanatic, in the midst of his atrocity, retains a mournfully venerable radiance.
Les Miserables	without suspecting it, javert, in his formidable happiness, was worthy of pity, like every ignorant man who triumphs; nothing could be so poignant and terrible as this face, in which was displayed all that may be called the wickedness of good.
Les Miserables	chapter iv.
Les Miserables	authority resumes its rights.
Les Miserables	fantine had not seen javert since the day when the mayor tore her out of his clutches, and her sickly brain could form no other thought but that he had come to fetch her.
Les Miserables	she could not endure his frightful face: she felt herself dying.
Les Miserables	she buried her face in her hands, and cried with agony,--  "monsieur madeleine, save me!"
Les Miserables	jean valjean--we will not call him otherwise in future--had risen, and said to fantine in his gentlest, calmest voice,--  "do not be alarmed: he has not come for you."
Les Miserables	then he turned to javert and said,--  "i know what you want."
Les Miserables	and javert answered,--  "come, make haste--"  there was something savage and frenzied in the accent that accompanied these words; no orthographer could write it down, for it was no longer human speech, but a roar.
Les Miserables	he did not behave as usual, he did not enter into the matter or display his warrant.
Les Miserables	to him jean valjean was a sort of mysterious combatant, a dark wrestler with whom he had been struggling for five years, and had been unable to throw.
Les Miserables	this arrest was not a beginning but an end, and he confined himself to saying, "come, make haste."
Les Miserables	while speaking thus, he did not advance: he merely darted at jean valjean the look which he threw out as a grapple, and with which he violently drew wretches to him.
Les Miserables	it was this look which fantine had felt pierce to her marrow two months before.
Les Miserables	on hearing javert's roar, fantine opened her eyes again; but the mayor was present, so what had she to fear?
Les Miserables	javert walked into the middle of the room and cried,--  "well, are you coming?"
Les Miserables	the unhappy girl looked around her.
Les Miserables	no one was present but the nun and the mayor; to whom, then, could this humiliating remark be addressed?
Les Miserables	only to herself.
Les Miserables	she shuddered.
Les Miserables	then she saw an extraordinary thing,--so extraordinary that nothing like it had ever appeared in the darkest delirium of fever.
Les Miserables	she saw the policeman javert seize the mayor by the collar, and she saw the mayor bow his head.
Les Miserables	it seemed to her as if the end of the world had arrived.
Les Miserables	"monsieur le maire!"
Les Miserables	fantine screamed.
Les Miserables	javert burst into a laugh,--that frightful laugh which showed all his teeth.
Les Miserables	"there is no monsieur le maire here."
Les Miserables	jean valjean did not attempt to remove the hand that grasped his collar; he said,--  "javert--"  javert interrupted him: "call me monsieur the inspector."
Les Miserables	"i should like to say a word to you in private, sir," jean valjean continued.
Les Miserables	"speak up," javert answered; "people talk aloud to me."
Les Miserables	jean valjean went on in a low voice,--  "it is a request i have to make of you."
Les Miserables	"i tell you to speak up."
Les Miserables	"but it must only be heard by yourself--"  "what do i care for that?
Les Miserables	i am not listening!"
Les Miserables	jean valjean turned to him and said rapidly, and in a very low voice,--  "grant me three days,--three days to go and fetch this unhappy woman's child!
Les Miserables	i will pay whatever you ask, and you can accompany me if you like."
Les Miserables	"you must be joking," javert cried.
Les Miserables	"why, i did not think you such a fool!
Les Miserables	you ask three days of me that you may bolt!
Les Miserables	you say that it is to fetch this girl's brat!
Les Miserables	ah, ah, that is rich, very rich!"
Les Miserables	fantine had a tremor.
Les Miserables	"my child!"
Les Miserables	she exclaimed,--"to go and fetch my child?
Les Miserables	then she is not here!
Les Miserables	sister, answer me,--where is cosette?
Les Miserables	i want my child!
Les Miserables	monsieur madeleine, m. le maire!"
Les Miserables	javert stamped his foot.
Les Miserables	"there's the other beginning now; will you be quiet, wench?
Les Miserables	a devil's own country, where galley-slaves are magistrates, and street-walkers are nursed like countesses.
Les Miserables	well, well, it will be altered now, and it's time for it."
Les Miserables	he looked fixedly at fantine, and added, as he took a fresh hold of jean valjean's cravat, shirt, and coat-collar,--  "i tell you there is no m. madeleine and no monsieur le maire; but there is a robber, a brigand, a convict of the name of jean valjean, and i've got him,--that's what there is!"
Les Miserables	fantine rose, supporting herself on her stiffened arms and hands; she looked at jean valjean; she looked at javert; she looked at the nun; she opened her mouth as if to speak, but there was a rattle in her throat, her teeth chattered, she stretched out her arms, convulsively opening her hands, clutching like a drowning man, and then suddenly fell back on the pillow.
Les Miserables	her head struck against the bed-head, and fell back on her breast with gaping mouth and open eyes.
Les Miserables	she was dead.
Les Miserables	jean valjean laid his hand on that one of javert's which held him, opened it as if it had been a child's hand, and then said to javert,--  "you have killed this woman."
Les Miserables	"enough of this!"
Les Miserables	javert shouted furiously.
Les Miserables	"i am not here to listen to abuse, so you can save your breath.
Les Miserables	there is a guard down below, so come quickly, or i shall handcuff you."
Les Miserables	there was in the corner of the room an old iron bedstead in a bad condition, which the sisters used as a sofa when they were sitting up at night.
Les Miserables	jean valjean went to this bed, tore off in a twinkling the head piece,--an easy thing for muscles like his,--seized the supporting bar, and looked at javert.
Les Miserables	javert recoiled to the door.
Les Miserables	jean valjean, with the iron bar in his hand, walked slowly up to fantine's bed; when he reached it, he turned and said to javert in a scarcely audible voice,--  "i would advise you not to disturb me just at present."
Les Miserables	one thing is certain,--javert trembled.
Les Miserables	he thought of going to fetch the guard, but jean valjean might take advantage of the moment to escape.
Les Miserables	he therefore remained, clutched his stick by the small end, and leaned against the door-post, without taking his eyes off jean valjean.
Les Miserables	the latter rested his elbow on the bedstead, and his forehead on his hand, and began contemplating fantine, who lay motionless before him.
Les Miserables	he remained thus, absorbed and silent, and evidently not thinking of anything else in the world.
Les Miserables	on his face and in his attitude there was only an indescribable pity.
Les Miserables	after a few minutes passed in this reverie, he stooped over fantine and spoke to her in a low voice.
Les Miserables	what did he say to her?
Les Miserables	what could this outcast man say to this dead woman?
Les Miserables	no one on earth heard the words, but did that dead woman hear them?
Les Miserables	there are touching illusions, which are perhaps sublime realities.
Les Miserables	one thing is indubitable, that sister simplice, the sole witness of what took place, has frequently declared that at the moment when jean valjean whispered in fantine's ear, she distinctly saw an ineffable smile playing round her pale lips and in her vague eyeballs, which were full of the amazement of the tomb.
Les Miserables	jean valjean took fantine's head in his hands, and laid it on the pillow, as a mother might have done to a child.
Les Miserables	then he tied the strings of her nightgown, and thrust her hair under her cap.
Les Miserables	when this was done, he closed her eyes.
Les Miserables	fantine's face at this moment seemed strangely illumined, for death is the entrance into brilliant light.
Les Miserables	fantine's hand was hanging out of bed; jean valjean knelt down by this hand, gently raised and kissed it.
Les Miserables	then he rose and turned to javert,--  "now i am at your service."
Les Miserables	chapter v.   a very proper tomb.
Les Miserables	javert placed jean valjean in the town jail.
Les Miserables	the arrest of m. madeleine produced an extraordinary commotion in m----, but it is sad to have to say that nearly everybody abandoned him on hearing that he was a galley-slave.
Les Miserables	in less than two hours all the good he had done was forgotten, and he was only a galley-slave.
Les Miserables	it is but fair to say, though, that they did not yet know the details of the affair at arras.
Les Miserables	the whole day through, conversations like the following could be heard in all parts of the town:--  "don't you know?
Les Miserables	he is a liberated convict.--who is?--the mayor.--nonsense.
Les Miserables	m.
Les Miserables	madeleine?--yes.--really?--his name is not madeleine, but some hideous thing like béjean, bojean, boujean.--oh, my goodness--he has been arrested, and will remain in the town jail till he is removed.--removed!
Les Miserables	where to?--he will be tried at the assizes for a highway robbery which he formerly committed.--well, do you know, i always suspected that man, for he was too kind, too perfect, too devout.
Les Miserables	he refused the cross, and gave sous to all the little scamps he met.
Les Miserables	i always thought that there was some black story behind."
Les Miserables	the "drawing-rooms" greatly improved the occasion.
Les Miserables	an old lady, who subscribed to the _drapeau blanc_, made this remark, whose depth it is almost impossible to fathom,--  "well, i do not feel sorry at it, for it will be a lesson to the buonapartists."
Les Miserables	it is thus that the phantom which called itself m. madeleine faded away at m----; only three or four persons in the whole town remained faithful to his memory, and his old servant was one of them.
Les Miserables	on the evening of the same day this worthy old woman was sitting in her lodge, still greatly startled and indulging in sad thoughts.
Les Miserables	the factory had been closed all day, the gates were bolted, and the street was deserted.
Les Miserables	there was no one in the house but the two nuns, who were watching by fantine's body.
Les Miserables	toward the hour when m. madeleine was wont to come in, the worthy portress rose mechanically, took the key of m. madeleine's bed-room from a drawer, and the candlestick which he used at night to go up-stairs; then she hung the key on the nail from which he usually took it, and placed the candlestick by its side, as if she expected him.
Les Miserables	then she sat down again and began thinking.
Les Miserables	the poor old woman had done all this unconsciously.
Les Miserables	she did not break off her reverie for two or three hours, and then exclaimed: "only think of that!
Les Miserables	i have hung his key on the nail!"
Les Miserables	at this moment the window of the lodge was opened, a hand was passed through the opening, which seized the key and lit the candle by hers.
Les Miserables	the portress raised her eyes, and stood with gaping mouth, but she repressed the cry which was in her throat; for she recognized this hand, this arm, this coat-sleeve, as belonging to m. madeleine.
Les Miserables	it was some minutes ere she could speak, for she "was struck," as she said afterwards when describing the adventure.
Les Miserables	"good gracious, m. le maire!"
Les Miserables	she at length exclaimed, "i fancied--"  she stopped, for the end of the sentence would have been disrespectful to the first part.
Les Miserables	jean valjean was still monsieur le maire with her.
Les Miserables	he completed her thought.
Les Miserables	"that i was in prison?"
Les Miserables	he said.
Les Miserables	"i was so, but i pulled out a bar, leaped out, and here i am.
Les Miserables	i am going up to my room; go and fetch sister simplice, who doubtless is by the side of that poor woman."
Les Miserables	the old servant hastened to obey; he said nothing further to her, for he was quite sure that she would guard him better than he could himself.
Les Miserables	it was never known how he managed to get into the yard without having the gate opened.
Les Miserables	he always carried about him a master-key, which opened a little side door, but he must have been searched and this key taken from him.
Les Miserables	this point was not cleared up.
Les Miserables	he went up the stairs that led to his room, and on reaching the landing, left the candle on the top stair, closed his window and shutters, and then entered the room with the candle.
Les Miserables	this precaution was useful, for it will be remembered that his window could be noticed from the street.
Les Miserables	he took a glance around him, at his table, his chair, his bed, which had not been slept in for three nights.
Les Miserables	no trace of that night's disorder remained, for the portress "had done his room;" but she had picked out of the ashes and laid neatly on the table the two iron ends of the stick and the forty-sous piece, which was blackened by the fire.
Les Miserables	he took a sheet of paper, on which he wrote, "this is the two-franc piece stolen from little gervais to which i alluded in court," and he laid the coin on the paper, so that it should be the first thing seen on entering the room.
Les Miserables	he took from a drawer an old shirt which he tore up, and wrapped the two candlesticks in the rags.
Les Miserables	still, he displayed no haste or agitation, and while wrapping up the candlesticks he ate a piece of black bread,--probably the prison bread which he took with him on his escape.
Les Miserables	this fact was proved by the crumbs found on the boards when the authorities made an investigation at a later date.
Les Miserables	there were two gentle taps at the door.
Les Miserables	"come in," he said.
Les Miserables	it was sister simplice; she was pale, her eyes were red, and the candle she held shook in her hand.
Les Miserables	violent events of destiny have this peculiarity, that however perfect or cold we may be, they draw human nature out of our entrails and compel it to reappear on the surface.
Les Miserables	in the emotions of this day the nun had become a woman again; she had wept and was trembling.
Les Miserables	jean valjean had just finished writing some lines on a piece of paper, which he handed to the sister, with the remark, "sister, you will deliver this to the curé?"
Les Miserables	as the paper was open, she turned her eyes on it.
Les Miserables	"you may read it," he said.
Les Miserables	she read, "i request the curé to take charge of all that i leave here.
Les Miserables	he will be good enough to defray out of it the costs of my trial and the interment of the woman who died this morning.
Les Miserables	the rest will be for the poor."
Les Miserables	the sister attempted to speak, but could only produce a few inarticulate sounds: at length she managed to say,--  "do you not wish to see the poor unhappy girl for the last time, sir?"
Les Miserables	"no," he said; "i am pursued, and if i were to be arrested in her room it would disturb her."
Les Miserables	he had scarce said this, ere a great noise broke out on the staircase: they heard a tumult of ascending steps, and the old servant cry in her loudest and most piercing voice,--  "my good sir, i can take my oath that no one has come in here all day or all the evening, and i have not left my lodge once."
Les Miserables	a man answered,--  "but there is a light in that room."
Les Miserables	they recognized javert's voice.
Les Miserables	the room was so built that the door, on being thrown open, concealed a nook in the right-hand wall: jean valjean blew out the light and crept into the nook.
Les Miserables	sister simplice fell on her knees by the table, as the door opened and javert entered.
Les Miserables	the voices of several men and the protestations of the old portress could be heard.
Les Miserables	the nun did not raise her eyes: she was praying.
Les Miserables	her candle was on the chimney and gave but little light, and on noticing the nun, javert halted in great confusion.
Les Miserables	it will be remembered that the very basis of javert, his element, the air he breathed, was reverence for all authority: he was all of one piece, and allowed no objection or limitation.
Les Miserables	with him, of course, ecclesiastical authority was the highest of all: he was religious, superficial, and correct on this point as on all.
Les Miserables	in his eyes, a priest was a spirit that does not deceive, a nun a creature who does not sin.
Les Miserables	theirs were souls walled up against the world with only one door, which never opened except to let truth pass out.
Les Miserables	on noticing the sister, his first movement was to withdraw, but he had another duty too, which imperiously urged him in an opposite direction.
Les Miserables	his second impulse was to remain, and at least venture one question.
Les Miserables	sister simplice had never told a falsehood in her life: javert was aware of this, and especially revered her for it.
Les Miserables	"sister," he asked, "are you alone in the room?"
Les Miserables	there was a terrible moment, during which the old servant felt as if she were going to faint: the sister raised her eyes and said, "yes."
Les Miserables	"in that case," javert continued, "i beg your pardon for pressing you, but it is my duty,--you have not seen this evening a person, a man who has escaped and we are seeking,--that fellow of the name of jean valjean.
Les Miserables	have you seen him?"
Les Miserables	the sister answered "no."
Les Miserables	she had told two falsehoods, one upon the other, without hesitation, rapidly, as if devoting herself.
Les Miserables	"i beg your pardon," said javert; and he withdrew with a deep bow.
Les Miserables	oh, holy woman!
Les Miserables	it is many years since you were on this earth; you have rejoined in the light your sisters the virgins and your brothers the angels; may this falsehood be placed to your credit in paradise!
Les Miserables	the sister's assertion was so decisive for javert that he did not notice the singular fact of the candle just blown out, and which was still smoking on the table.
Les Miserables	an hour later a man, making his way through the fog, was hurrying away from m---- in the direction of paris.
Les Miserables	this man was jean valjean; and it was proved, by the testimony of two or three carriers who met him, that he was carrying a bundle and was dressed in a blouse.
Les Miserables	where did he procure this blouse from?
Les Miserables	it was never known; but a few days before, an old workman had died in the infirmary of the sailors, leaving only a blouse.
Les Miserables	it might have been that one.
Les Miserables	one last word about fantine.
Les Miserables	we have all one mother, the earth, and fantine was given back to that mother.
Les Miserables	the curé thought he was doing his duty, and perhaps did it, in keeping as much money for the poor as he possibly could out of what jean valjean left him.
Les Miserables	after all, who were the people interested?
Les Miserables	a convict and a street-walker: hence he simplified fantine's interment, and reduced it to what is called the "public grave."
Les Miserables	fantine was therefore interred in the free corner of the cemetery, which belongs to everybody and to nobody, and where the poor are lost.
Les Miserables	fortunately god knows where to look for a soul.
Les Miserables	fantine was laid in the darkness among a pile of promiscuous bones in the public grave.
Les Miserables	her tomb resembled her bed.
